Haimen: Widow Zhu's Home Robbed 90

In Yujia Village, the fourth district of Qidong, there is a widow named Zhu, whose husband died many years ago. In the eighteenth year of the Republic of China, she cohabited with Kai Dao, the younger brother of Pan Kaiqu, a giant bandit in Jiangbei. In the nineteenth year, Bandit Pan was executed, and Kai Dao escaped without a trace. All the silver dollars and valuables obtained by robbery were collected by Widow Zhu on his behalf, a considerable amount. Recently, bandits learned of this and went to rob her in groups at about 9 p.m. the day before yesterday. After entering the room, they first twisted and beat Zhu fiercely, forcing her to hand over the hidden silver. Zhu had no choice but to hand over a small box under the bed, containing 310 silver dollars and many gold and silver jewelry ornaments. The bandits, believing that their purpose had been achieved, left with a howl. Yesterday, Zhou, the police inspector in charge of the local public security sub-station, learned of this, went to investigate, and reported to the county government for investigation.

Pinghu: Doctor Robbed While Making a House Call 91

Shen Lanzhuang, a doctor outside the Dananmen, went to Sigufang the other day to introduce vaccination to someone. He was drinking tea and resting in a certain teahouse in Dazhaiqiao. Suddenly, an unknown rascal entered to make trouble. Shen, being alone and helpless, ran away from the back door. A moment later, the rascal caught up, knocked Shen down to the ground, and robbed him of the silver dollars around him and the gold ring on his hand. Shen returned to the city to report to the authorities. That night, it was discovered that the perpetrators were local hoodlums Cheng Lin, a barber, and Zhang Sanada. They were arrested and sent to the county today.

Local News

Ten Groups Held a Welcome Banquet for the American Economic Mission Last Night; Mission Leader Visited Key Chinese Figures in Shanghai Yesterday Morning; American Chamber of Commerce Also Hosted a Luncheon; Meeting to Discuss Business Matters This Afternoon 92

The American Economic Mission visited the reception committee chairman Zhang Jia'ao, Finance Minister Kong Xiangxi, Bank of China Chairman Zhu Ziwen, and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday morning. At noon, they attended a banquet hosted by the American Chamber of Commerce, while their families attended a banquet hosted by the Chinese Women's Association. In the evening, the reception committee and sixteen groups held a banquet in their honor, with a speech by Zhang Jia'ao. Later that night, they attended a dance hosted by the American University Club. A specialist meeting will be held this afternoon. Our Central News Agency reporter has compiled the following details:

Visiting Key Figures Yesterday morning, the head of the mission, Forbes, accompanied by Secretary Stoddert, visited key government figures and business leaders in Shanghai. Guo Bingwen from the reception committee accompanied them. At 9:00 a.m., they first visited Zhang Jia'ao, chairman of the reception committee, at his residence on Jessfield Road to express their gratitude and had a pleasant conversation. At around 10:00 a.m., they went to the Central Bank to call on Finance Minister Kong Xiangxi. At 10:30 a.m., they visited Song Ziwen at his private residence on Route Cardinal Mercier and had a long conversation. After 12:00 p.m., they visited the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, where they were warmly received by Yu Zuoting, Du Yuesheng, Chen Zeqing, Ke Ganchen, Ma Jiliang, Jin Runxiang, and over ten others from the chamber. They discussed matters for about half an hour before leaving.

American Community Banquet At noon, all members of the mission attended a luncheon hosted by the American Chamber of Commerce in Shanghai. The attendees were all prominent American expatriates in Shanghai, numbering about fifty. During the luncheon, the Vice-Chairman of the American Chamber of Commerce, Franklin, delivered a welcoming speech, stating that American expatriates in Shanghai should do their utmost to assist the mission during its stay in China and wished the mission success. Forbes, the head of the mission, responded by saying that the mission's purpose in China was to gather commercial data between the two countries and expressed his gratitude for the assistance of the chamber. At the same time, the Chinese Women's Association hosted a banquet for the mission's families at Mrs. Bei Zuyi's residence on Avenue Ferguson. Those present included Mrs. Stoddert, Mrs. Dillingham, Mrs. Wickham, Mrs. Hutchins, Mrs. Beikspe, and staff from the association, totaling forty-five people. The President of the Association, Mrs. Wen Yuqing, gave a welcoming speech, followed by a performance of Chinese music to add to the enjoyment. The guests and hosts had a lively and pleasant conversation.

Group Banquet Last night at 7:00 p.m., the reception committee, the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the China National Industries Association, the China International Trade Association, the Chinese Economic Society, the China National Committee of the International Chamber of Commerce, the Chinese Institute of Engineers, the Shanghai Banking Association, the China Institute in Pacific Relations, the Shanghai Money Dealers Association, the International Problem Research Association, the Shanghai Local Autonomy Association, the Shanghai YMCA, the China National Roads Association, the Chinese Students' Alliance, the China Aviation Association, and the Chinese Students Studying in America Association in Shanghai, a total of sixteen groups, held a welcome banquet at the International Recreation Club on Bubbling Well Road. All members of the mission and their families attended, along with senior officials from the Shanghai Municipal Government, bureau chiefs, Kong Xiangxi, Song Ziwen, Song Ziliang, Gu Shaochuan, Yu Qiaqing, Ding Wenjiang, Zhao Tiezhang, Wang Xiaolai, Du Yuesheng, Yu Zuoting, Zhang Xiaolin, Huang Jinrong, Lao Jingxiu, Wu Yunzhai, Wang Yunwu, Zhao Jinqing, Mu Ouchu, Li Fuxun, Xu Xinliu, Cao Yunxiang, Admiral Yabraham, Commander-in-Chief of the US Far East Fleet, US Consul General Cunningham, US Assessor Harmill, US Marine Corps Commander Barman, US Consul Davis, US High-Level Counselor Arno, and consuls from various countries, were invited to attend, with reception committee members hosting. Over three hundred people attended. The Datong Music Society also attended to perform classical music to enhance the atmosphere.

Chairman's Speech At the banquet, Chairman Zhang Jia'ao rose to speak, saying, "Tonight, various groups in this city related to international business and culture have jointly welcomed the American Economic Mission with a toast, hoping to strengthen the economic and business ties between the two major Pacific powers. On behalf of the various civil groups, I would like to express a few words to show our welcome. Aside from Mr. Dalai's small group visiting China in 1910, the United States has not had a large group of well-known figures from various fields, such as this mission. International trade relations rely on daily negotiations and the accumulation of goodwill. Since the commencement of trade between China and the United States, both sides have treated each other fairly and justly at all times and in all places, so there have been no political disputes, and Sino-American trade has continued to increase. Today, we have such a large delegation visiting our country, which can be seen as the culmination of decades of friendly relations. On the American side, they understand that the Chinese people crave peace and seek international economic development, and they wish to further shake hands with our people. On the Chinese side, we firmly believe that the American people's spirit of upholding fairness and justice remains consistent. We deeply desire an opportunity to express our deeper goodwill. Today, we have this good opportunity to gather together, and not only is a peaceful atmosphere filling the room, but also the hope for further economic cooperation in the future will surely fill the hearts of everyone present. In this time of extreme global economic downturn, ordinary people often doubt whether an international economic mission is appropriate at this time, and even doubt whether the mission's purpose is solely to promote the sale of one-sided goods. These are all superficial views. They do not understand that economic cooperation must first involve understanding each other's economic weaknesses. Otherwise, merely knowing how to utilize each other's strengths without knowing how to support each other's weaknesses will lead to resentment and blame when one country's weakness cannot receive assistance from the other party. This will eventually exhaust the benefits of utilizing each other's strengths. Today, the economic weaknesses of various countries have been revealed due to the impact of the downturn. If one wants to know the weaknesses of the Chinese economy, now is indeed the most appropriate time. Not only is it easy to discern the inherent weaknesses in China's economic foundation, but it is also easy to see the weaknesses of China's inability to resist the impact of the economic policies of various countries due to the global downturn. Our people naturally do not want to hide their weaknesses, just as a patient does not need to conceal their symptoms from others. Although there are various reasons for the global downturn, the narrow nationalistic economic policies are the root cause. All countries want to increase exports and decrease imports, resulting in more and more obstacles being set up in international trade, and the purchasing power of all countries is simultaneously declining. Even the United States, with its strong economic power, cannot escape the influence of global trends, and various measures to reverse the downturn have been tested one by one. Therefore, the recognition of the necessity for international cooperation to achieve common prosperity is deeper than that of any other country. Today, the gentlemen of the American Economic Mission can reveal the weaknesses of our country's economy to our people and discuss them together through methods of mutual assistance and cooperation. In the future, after returning to their country, they can further convey the location of China's economic weaknesses and the necessity and methods of mutual assistance and cooperation to the American government and people. Then, the benefits of this trip to the economic relations between China and the United States will be far from superficial. The gentlemen of your mission are all experienced and knowledgeable. Once you have investigated the economic situation in China, it will not be difficult to see it at a glance. We should not wait for the various groups present tonight to point it out. Before your mission departs, I would like to contribute one or two special features of China's economic situation for your reference, which I believe the gentlemen would be willing to hear. First, the urgency of China's economic construction has been commonly recognized by the government and the people, and the efforts of the government and the people in carrying out the work have already yielded considerable results. China's modern construction began after the establishment of the National Government. Recently, with Commander-in-Chief Chiang's efforts to suppress the communists and restore the countryside, it is even more urgent to realize that the progress of construction cannot be delayed any longer. To reverse prosperity, there is a greater need for large-scale construction. Once the communist bandits are eliminated and disasters are reduced, the purchasing power of the Chinese people will increase dramatically. It would not be difficult to double or multiply the current import of one billion silver dollars. At that time, China may become a major market for the world to absorb goods. Today, the materials needed for economic construction and the increased purchasing power of the people after construction are sufficient to increase the China trade of various countries. In other words, countries that participate in or assist China's economic construction are promoting their China trade. China will also be willing to purchase goods from any country that is interested in assisting China's economic construction. There is one more thing I can tell the gentlemen: the Chinese government, knowing that economic construction relies on foreign aid, must consolidate its external credibility. Since Finance Minister Kong took office, he has worked hard to consolidate external credibility, and now he has seen results and received good feedback from industrialists from various countries. Second, China is the only country in the world that purely uses silver. All of China's economic life is closely related to the price of silver. In the past, the rise and fall of silver prices were determined by the needs and supply of China and India. The more China's tangible and intangible exports, the more silver is needed. The more silver China needs, the higher the price of silver rises. As the price of silver rises, prices in China rise, and tangible exports decrease until the demand for silver decreases and the price of silver gradually flattens. Since the implementation of the US silver purchase policy, the price of silver has been artificially raised. As a result, China's silver price, based on the principle of natural supply and demand, has completely broken the trade monetary system, and everything is affected by it. The Chinese people cannot help but sigh at the ignorance of the American senators about the actual situation in China. At this critical juncture, the gentlemen of your mission have personally come to investigate. After returning to your country in the future, you will be able to convey the real situation in China to the government and people of your country and try to reduce the adverse effects on China. Then, this silver problem, which currently seems to be a very unpleasant matter in the economic relations between the two countries, or even this problem of conflicting interests, may discover a common point of cooperation and add a link to the economic relations between the two countries. However, the transformation of this direction depends on the efforts of the economic groups of the two countries, and the efforts of your mission are especially effective. I hope that the gentlemen of your mission will not think that I am being presumptuous in mentioning this matter. I would be very grateful. The gentlemen of your mission have traveled far to visit, and there must be many things you want to hear. Tonight, all the groups present are willing to provide as much information as possible so that the real situation in our country can be disclosed to you, so that the business between China and the United States can be further advanced and the friendship between the two countries can become even stronger, which is what we all deeply hope for."

Mission Leader's Response Forbes, the head of the American Economic Mission, then rose to speak in response, saying, "Our mission has come to China to investigate, and we are honored to have received the warm hospitality of your government authorities, your reception committee, and business leaders, and to have been given guidance. Our various investigation efforts are currently underway to promote the prosperity of trade between the two countries. We are very grateful for the assistance and guidance we have received from all sectors. We offer our thanks and wish all of you good health."

This is a business discussion, and the content will not be publicly disclosed. At the same time, mission leader Forbes will go to the Capital Hotel to attend the meeting of the Pan-Pacific Association and deliver a speech. At 5:00 p.m., Finance Minister Kong will host a tea party at his private residence on Avenue Petain, inviting celebrities from various Chinese and foreign circles to accompany him. It is said that the members of the amateur music group Huaguang Music Association will participate and perform ancient Chinese music and the latest ensemble pieces to add to the enjoyment. Leaders of Chinese Businesses and Banks Mortgage Loans Reach 20 Million; China Alone Makes 9 Million, and the Jiaotong and Four Banks Make About 5 Million; The China, Central, and Jiaotong Banks Jointly Lend 8 Million Yuan; The Banking Industry Has Implemented the Extension of Long-Term Loans Due at the End of the Quarter 96

The Shun Pao reports that recently in Shanghai, with the end of the quarter approaching, and due to the successive declarations of liquidation by Yongxing and Tongtai exchange houses, instability has been caused in the market. However, this situation has been fully eliminated after the authorities have tried their best to maintain it, and the major Chinese banks such as China and Jiaotong have provided substantial assistance by implementing large-scale mortgage loans. According to inquiries made by the Shun Pao reporter to the major banks, the total amount of mortgage loans recently released by the banks has exceeded 20 million yuan. China Bank has released about 9 million yuan, the China, Central, and Jiaotong Banks have jointly released about 8 million yuan, the Jiaotong and Four Banks' reserve has released about 5 million yuan, and other banks such as Shanghai, Zhongnan, Jin Cheng, and Dalu have also released more than 1 million yuan each. The interest rate is mostly within 2 cents per thousand yuan per day.

The Banking Industry Implements Long-Term Rollovers There are only four days left until the end of the quarter. According to the reporter's investigation yesterday, this difficulty can indeed be safely overcome. Of the 50 million yuan in long-term loans due, except for the hardware merchants who have repaid half of them, and the out-of-town merchants who have repaid them due to Yongfeng's collection of accounts, the remaining 40 million yuan can mostly be rolled over as usual. However, the interest rate must be appropriately increased, roughly by about half a yuan higher than the previous period. The interest rate for the previous period was 8 yuan. As for those that have already been transacted, the money industry has not heard of any. The banking industry has recently approved the rollover of several large loans. For example, Zhejiang Industrial, Shanghai, China, and Jiaotong Banks jointly lent about 500,000 yuan to Houfeng Company, with a monthly interest rate of 8.5%; China Bank lent 1.2 million yuan to the timber industry, with an interest rate of 8.75%; and China Bank lent 300,000 yuan to the pig industry, with an interest rate of 8.75%. Therefore, it is expected that in the next three days, large amounts of loans will continue to be rolled over. Therefore, yesterday, the public morale in the city became more stable.

The Money Market Has Eased Yesterday, the trading situation in the money market has eased even further. The premium for delayed delivery has fallen to below 25 cents, but the call loan rate has risen by several points compared to the previous day. The interest rate on mortgage loans made by the money industry is only 2 cents per day, so the higher call loan rate in the market is expected. It has almost returned to its original state. It is reported that most of the firms with shortages have now found ways to raise sufficient funds. Therefore, the difficulty at the end of the quarter can be safely overcome.

After Siam's Harsh Treatment of Overseas Chinese, the Reactions of Various Circles in Our Country; the Food Industry Advocates No Longer Purchasing Siamese Rice; the Overseas Chinese Affairs Sector Hopes to Expedite the Conclusion of a Sino-Siamese Commercial Treaty 97

The Central News Agency reports that the various harsh measures implemented by the Siamese authorities against overseas Chinese have caused them great hardship. Therefore, people in our country have expressed dissatisfaction with the Siamese authorities. The Central News Agency reporter has interviewed various parties to explore their attitudes, as follows:

Opinions of the Food Industry China and Siam are neighboring countries, and there is a very close relationship in business. According to a tycoon in the food industry in Shanghai, Siam is an agricultural country, and rice is its main product, accounting for two-thirds of the total export value. The number of Siamese rice shipped to China is not small. Since the overseas Chinese He Defu returned to China last year and had contacts with the Shanghai food merchants, the quantity of imports has increased sharply. From August of last year to March of this year, the value of Siamese rice shipped to Shanghai has reached 10 million yuan. Since the Siamese authorities cannot be good neighbors and impose various harsh measures on our overseas Chinese, our merchants can only give them an economic blow. Although our country has suffered from natural and man-made disasters in recent years, resulting in poor agricultural production, we still have to rely on foreign countries. However, in terms of foreign rice, not purchasing Siamese rice will have no impact on our country. Moreover, recently, due to the economic recession in our country, Siamese rice has no market in our country. Therefore, if the Siamese authorities do not change their attitude, they will definitely no longer purchase Siamese rice.

News from the Overseas Chinese Affairs Sector According to the Overseas Chinese Affairs sector, the authorities should urgently conclude a Sino-Siamese commercial treaty to establish a proper national relationship between our country and Siam. Siam was originally a tributary state of ours, and even in the recent past, many nationals occupied important positions in the government of that country. Therefore, the number of our overseas Chinese who have gone to that country to do business has reached 3 million. However, in recent years, the Siamese authorities have been manipulated by the great powers. Therefore, although there have been moves to conclude a treaty between China and Siam, it has not been realized due to the lack of sincerity of the Siamese authorities. However, in terms of the relationship between the two countries, at least a minimum commercial treaty should be concluded as soon as possible. The Siamese authorities should change their attitude, considering their own interests and the importance of their relationship with China, to establish a friendly relationship between China and Siam.

Yuxing Steamer Encountered Danger; Salvaged Back to Shanghai by Jardine Matheson 101

The Zhaoxing Company's Yuxing steamer, with a deadweight of 1,599 tons, fully loaded export goods on the morning of the 25th of this month. It sailed to ports such as Longkou, Niuzhuang, and Tianjin. The majority of the cargo was 6,380 bags of white rice, 3,000 pieces of fertilizer, and over 10,000 bags of flour. Other items included miscellaneous goods like foreign cloth, tea, and cigarettes. All the ship's holds were fully loaded, and the weight carried had reached the waterline. The value of the entire ship's cargo was over 200,000 yuan.

Encountered Danger Near Sheshan: At 6:00 PM, approximately 10 nautical miles south of Sheshan, at 122 degrees 20 minutes east longitude and 32 degrees 34 minutes north latitude, the propeller of the propulsion engine suddenly fell off, causing the ship to lose its ability to move. It was left to drift in the sea, with no way to remedy the situation. The ship was heavily laden and deep in the water. If a major storm were to occur, the consequences would be unimaginable. The shipowner, a Japanese national, was at a loss, and the entire crew was extremely anxious. They immediately sent a telegram to Shanghai to report the emergency and request assistance.

Tugboat Rescue: After receiving the telegram that evening, the company decided overnight to hire the large Jardine Matheson tugboat "Saucy" from this port. It set out at 1:00 AM yesterday morning, rushed to the waters off Sheshan, and towed the ship back to Shanghai. A telegram was received yesterday afternoon stating that the "Saucy" tugboat had successfully towed the Yuxing steamer and was en route to Shanghai. It was expected to arrive in port around 7:00 PM that evening.

Shanghai Telephone Bureau Actively Arranging; Traffic Inquiry Desk to Expand Existing Inquiry Room; Implementation Decided on the First of Next Month 102

According to the Dagong News Agency, the Shanghai Telephone Bureau originally established an inquiry room for users to inquire about matters and request repairs. For the South City, Zhabei, Longhua areas, dial "29"; for Pudong, Jiangwan, Zhenru, and Wusong areas, dial "50." The scope of inquiries was limited to standard time and repair of lines and machines. Now that the bureau has been ordered by the Ministry of Transportation to establish an inquiry desk, the original inquiry room will be expanded, the number of staff answering inquiries will be increased, and shifts will be scheduled.

Collecting Materials: The bureau has sent letters to the local post office, telegraph bureau, wireless telegraph station, China National Aviation Corporation, Eurasia Aviation Corporation, Jinghu and Huhangyong Railway Administrations, China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, municipal ferries, commercial steamship companies, and the Minhang, Hutai, Husong, Shangnan, and long-distance bus companies, as well as entertainment venues and hotels, to collect traffic information for answering user inquiries. This includes various mailing fees, travel and meal prices, and schedules. The standard time of the Municipal Public Works Bureau will be used as the standard. Subsequently, all traffic schedules, fire alarms, etc., will be immediately answered by the inquiry desk.

Implementation at the Beginning of the Month: The bureau is actively arranging the citywide traffic inquiry desk and has decided to implement it starting on May 1st. All users within the city, regardless of whether they are in the South City, Zhabei, Longhua, Jiangwan, Zhenru, Pudong, city center, or Wusong districts, will not be charged for inquiries. However, users who inquire using long-distance or public telephones will still be required to pay the call fee according to regulations.

Art Exhibition: Preview on the 19th; Antiquities Scheduled to Ship to England on June 8th 103

Yesterday (the 26th) was the 19th day of the Shanghai preview of the International Exhibition of Chinese Art in London. The number of people from all walks of life attending the exhibition was very high, and they all had very good reviews of the various antiquities on display. The various pieces of news obtained yesterday are listed as follows:

Director Lei Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday, Adding a Catalog of Antiquities

Lei Zhen, the executive director of the exhibition, arrived in Shanghai by train from Nanjing yesterday and immediately went to the exhibition hall to preside over matters. Mr. Lei also brought two large boxes of selected archaeological items from the Archaeological Division of the Institute of History and Philology of the Academia Sinica, totaling eleven items. After arriving at the exhibition hall, he immediately opened the boxes, organized the items, and handed them over to the second group for display. The Archaeological Division of the Institute of History and Philology of the Academia Sinica also added eleven selected items, as well as a photograph and a tomb inscription, which were added for exhibition at the special request of the British selection committee. The catalog is recorded below: (1) Lower part of a stone-carved human figure; (2) Edge of a carved white pottery vessel, with the ears shaped like taotie. The above two items were unearthed from the Yin Ruins. (3) Four pieces of black pottery fragments, unearthed from Chengziya. (4) One high-footed plate. (5) Two four-eared jars. (6) Two cups, as well as a full photograph of the Bu Ren tomb and a rubbing of the Bu Ren tomb inscription. These antiquities are of great value in archaeology.

Date of Shipment of Antiquities to England; Explanation of Archaeological Selections

The date for shipping these antiquities to London for the exhibition in England has been set for June 8th. They will be transported by the British warship Suffolk. The exhibition is currently in contact with the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to discuss borrowing a loading and unloading wharf. Explanations of the archaeological selections regarding divination oracle bones, oracle bone characters, deer head inscriptions, stone knives, stone axes, and bone hairpins have already been reported in this newspaper. Now, the explanations for bone tools, arrowheads, spears, axes are recorded below: (7) Bone tools. There are more bone-made tools preserved from the Yin Ruins than other types. Seven types are shown to demonstrate their general uses. (1) Bone knife: One end has a hole, and the other end has a blade; it is extremely thin and used for cutting and scraping. (2) Bone wedge: The end is extremely thick, and the end has a blade; it is used for splitting small objects. (3) Bone awl: One end is sharp, and the other end is slightly scraped. (4) Bone nail: One end is thick and pointed, and the middle part is raised, resembling a nail. (5) Bone awl: One end is sharp, and the other end is flattened. (6) Bone perch: One end has a square head, with the edge raised as a grasping part; the other end has a blade, used for carving livestock. (7) Bone perch: One end has a square head with a hole, and the other end is curved like a stream, used for wine. (8) Arrowheads: There are two types of arrowheads unearthed from the Yin Ruins: bronze and bone. The shapes of the bone arrowheads vary greatly and can be divided into four types: 1. Conical; 2. Flat; 3. Double-edged; 4. Three-edged. The third type is the most common. There is only one type of bronze arrowhead, which belongs to the third type, but the size varies. Twenty selected pieces, ten bone and ten bronze, slightly demonstrate the general changes. (9) Spears, lances, axes: Spears and lances were the most prevalent weapons during the Yin and Shang periods, used for horizontal strikes and direct thrusts. The shape of the spears is very similar to the spears of the third phase of the European Bronze Age. Hollow-headed bronze axes also appeared during this period. Six selected types, three from the Yin Ruins, one from Xincun in Junxian, an object from the early Western Zhou dynasty, and one purchased in Anyang, an object from the middle Zhou dynasty, are placed here to demonstrate the changes in spear shapes.

Xue's Visit Report

Someone named Xue Quan once published a report on visiting the London Chinese Art Exhibition. The preview exhibition, held at the old site of the Bank of China at 22 Bund, Shanghai, displayed over 900 pieces of antiquities from various dynasties to the public. Its significance for national education and culture is extremely important. I visited the exhibition hall for a whole day on April 26th. I will briefly describe the general situation to readers: (1) Bronze Ware Section: The exhibition displayed a total of 108 pieces of bronze ware, including 60 pieces from the Palace Museum, 36 pieces from the Antiquities Exhibition Office, 8 pieces from the Henan Provincial Museum, and 4 pieces from the Anhui Provincial Library. The period ranges from the Yin and Shang dynasties, through the Western Zhou, Spring and Autumn, and Warring States periods, to the Han dynasty. They are divided into four categories: cooking utensils and tableware, containers, warming utensils and drinking vessels, ordinary utensils, and musical instruments. Among the cooking utensils and tableware, there are li, yan, ding, gui, dun, fu, dou, etc. Among the warming utensils and drinking vessels, there are jue, hu, yi, he, jue, zhi, gu, zun, etc. Among the ordinary utensils, there are pan, jian, yu, yi, lian, deng, etc. Among the musical instruments, there are zhong, bo, zheng, etc. Viewing these bronze wares allows one to imagine the daily life and production skills of the people in the past. The value of these bronze wares and their inscriptions in historical materials is self-evident. (2) Archaeological Selections Section: The archaeological selections included a total of 111 pieces of antiquities, all selected and sent by the Archaeological Division of the Institute of History and Philology of the Academia Sinica. These include 99 pieces unearthed from the Yin Ruins, 2 pieces from Xincun in Junxian, 1 piece purchased from the Anyang antique market, 4 pieces unearthed from Chengziya, and 5 funerary objects from the Sui Dynasty gentleman Bu Ren's tomb. They are divided into 14 categories: oracle bones for divination, oracle bone characters, deer head inscriptions, stone knives, stone axes, bone hairpins, various bone tools, arrowheads, spears, axes, bronze wares, fragments, bronze molds, bone carvings, ivory carvings, stone carvings, and refined pottery and black pottery. The arrangement is orderly and extremely convenient for viewing. The ancient culture seems to be brilliantly presented. (3) Rare Ancient Books Section: There were a total of 50 ancient books, selected and sent by the National Peiping Library. There are manuscripts from the Six Dynasties, engraved books from the Five Dynasties, printed books from the Northern Song Dynasty, printed books from the Southern Song Dynasty, engraved books from the Jin Dynasty, engraved books from the Yuan Dynasty, engraved books from the Ming Dynasty, fine transcribed books, engraved books from the Qing Dynasty, books printed in vermilion and black, books printed in five colors, books printed with copper movable type, woodblock prints, and butterfly-bound books. They are ancient in color and fragrance, and the copying and engraving are all exquisite. (4) Calligraphy and Painting Section: There were a total of 175 pieces of calligraphy and painting, including 5 pieces from the Antiquities Exhibition Office and 170 pieces from the Palace Museum. The period ranges from the Tang Dynasty, through the Five Dynasties, Song, Yuan, and Ming Dynasties, to the Qing Dynasty. There are silk paintings, paper paintings, colored paintings, cloth paintings, meticulous paintings, bold paintings, small characters, large characters, regular script, and running script. Paintings account for nine-tenths of the total, while calligraphy accounts for only one-tenth. They are further distinguished by the objects depicted, including figures, portraits of emperors and empresses, landscapes, flowers, insects and birds, still lifes, scenes, and close-ups. Calligraphers include Cai Junmo, Su Dongpo, Huang Tingjian, Zhu Yuanzhang, Zhao Mengfu, Shen Can, Wen Zhengming, Dong Qichang, and Emperor Gaozong of the Qing Dynasty. Painters include Dong Beiyuan, Juran, Li Cheng, Fan Kuan, Huang Gongwang, Wang Shimin, Li Zhaodao, Liu Songnian, Qiu Ying, Ma Yuan, Xia Gui, Ma Hezhi, Zhao Mengfu, Chen Hongshou, Diao Guangyin, Qian Xuan, and Zou Yigui, among dozens of others. There are horizontal scrolls, long scrolls, and large-scale paintings. The works of important artists from various schools are generally complete, which can be described as a grand spectacle. Furthermore, the best of the paintings are enough to make the viewer feel detached from reality and merge with the painting, as if placed in a landscape of mountains and forests, lingering and reluctant to leave. (5) Porcelain Section: There were a total of 352 pieces of porcelain, all selected and sent by the Palace Museum. Famous porcelains from various dynasties since the Song Dynasty are generally complete. Among them are the Ding, Jun, Guan, Longquan, Ge, and Jianyang kilns of the Song Dynasty; the Guan kiln of Nanjing, the Jizhou, Yuyao, Yuhang, Xianghu Suburban Altar Guan, and Guang kilns; the Suzhou and Pingding kilns of the Jin Dynasty; the Peng, Shufu, and Linchuan kilns of the Yuan Dynasty; the Chuzhou, Dehua, Guang, Yongle, Xuande, Chenghua, Hongzhi, Jiajing, Longqing, Wanli, Jingdezhen, Zhou, and Hugong kilns of the Ming Dynasty; and the Kangxi, Yongzheng, and Qianlong kilns of the Qing Dynasty. According to the type of porcelain, there are cups, bottles, boxes, zun, censers, bowls, basins, saucers, plates, dishes, gu, tubes, armrests, vases, flower holders, pots, brushes, yan, chan, dun, spittoons, pillows, jars, seals, fang, boxes, weng, incense burners, tanks, ding, yu, chu, lingzhi, flower sprinklers, clocks, inkstones, mountain crowns, etc. Famous porcelains from all over the world are gathered in one room, arranged in chronological order, and publicly exhibited. It is truly a grand event. (6) Jade Ware Section: There were a total of 62 pieces of jade ware, plus 1 piece of crystal, 2 pieces of agate, 1 piece of Qingtian stone, 1 piece of realgar, 2 pieces of rhinoceros horn, and 1 piece of silverware, totaling 70 pieces. Among them, 5 pieces are from the Antiquities Exhibition Office, and 65 pieces are from the Palace Museum. The jade includes old jade, white jade, yellow jade, jasper, ink jade, celadon jade, and emerald jade. They are made into gui, qiong, cong, huang, long, rings, yuan, fish, fu, qi, pixie, guang, cups, basins, knives, geese, square pendants, zun, pot bottles, bowls, stoves, yu, seals, brush holders, shepherds, incense burners, gui, boxes, screen inserts, and mountain ornaments. Agate is made into red agate flower inserts and agate Buddha hands. Qingtian stone is made into seals, realgar is made into mountain ornaments, rhinoceros horn is made into guang cups, and silver is made into silver raft cups. The workmanship is exquisite, the shapes are strange, the jade is smooth and lustrous, and the carving is absolutely exquisite. The treasure light shines in all directions, which is enough to make the viewers appreciate them endlessly. (7) Embroidery Section: There were a total of 29 pieces of embroidery, including 26 pieces of silk and 3 pieces of embroidery. 1 piece is from the Antiquities Exhibition Office, and 28 pieces are from the Palace Museum. The period ranges from the Song Dynasty, through the Yuan and Ming Dynasties, to the Qing Dynasty. The silk includes flowers, birds, figures, landscapes, and calligraphy. The embroidery includes Avalokiteśvara, the White House, and the Four Joys of Spring. The painting and shaping are lifelike. Such fine products are truly not easy to see. (8) Folding Fan Section: There were a total of 20 folding fans, all from the Ming Dynasty, selected and sent by the Palace Museum. There are paintings by Fan Qian, Shang Xi, Tang Yin, Qiu Ying, Zhou Chen, Wen Zhengming, Wen Boren, Lu Zhi, Dong Qichang, Chen Yu, Zhao Mi, Zhao Wenshu, Tan Zhiyi, Zhao Zuo, Li Shida, Ma Fushi, and Kang Zhenzhi, and calligraphy by Dong Qichang, Wen Zhengming, Han Daoheng, and Wang Zhizheng. The fan bones are made of bamboo, ivory, and palm wood. The calligraphy and painting are exquisite and extremely elegant. (9) Cloisonné Section: There were a total of 16 pieces of cloisonné, from the Ming and Qing Dynasties, selected and sent by the Palace Museum. They include bottles, gu, yu, plates, jars, rang, pots, and bowls. The workmanship is smooth and lustrous, and the paintings are exquisite and detailed. (10) Carved Red Lacquer Section: Carved red lacquer is also known as lacquer carving. There were a total of 5 pieces, all from the Ming Dynasty, selected and sent by the Palace Museum. There are plates, piers, and boxes. Among them, the embroidered pier is the largest, about a foot high, and the surface is nearly a foot wide. The round box carved with the character "Spring" is the most exquisite. The carving is extremely fine, and the patterns are quite rich in pattern painting style. (11) Furniture Section: There were a total of 3 pieces of furniture, including an emperor's throne, a surrounding screen, and a rosewood desk, all objects used by the emperor, selected and sent by the Palace Museum. The throne is very large and can seat two people. The surrounding screen is placed behind the seat. The rosewood painting desk, formerly known as Liu Yong's table, is carved with various calligraphy and paintings all around. Viewing this can give one a slight understanding of the emperor's situation when he was in court. (12) Stationery Section: There were a total of 16 pieces of stationery, including brushes, brush holders, ink, ink beds, seal paste boxes, seals, inkstones, brush holders, water vessels, bottles, armrests, etc., all objects used by the emperor, selected and sent by the Palace Museum. Each piece is made of jade, bone, carved lacquer, boxwood, or porcelain, all of which are extremely exquisite. The above are the various antiquities on display, totaling 955 pieces, including 735 pieces from the Palace Museum, 111 pieces from the Sino-British Research Institute, 50 pieces from the Peiping Library, 47 pieces from the Antiquities Exhibition Office, 8 pieces from the Henan Provincial Museum, and 4 pieces from the Anhui Provincial Library. After completing the viewing, I will briefly describe my feelings as follows: China has a culture of more than 4,000 years. In addition to the records in books, we rely on antiquities to observe the living conditions, working skills, artistic thoughts, and the efforts of our ancestors at that time. Therefore, appreciating old objects is not only about the value of the old objects themselves, but also about the culture reflected by the old objects at that time. It is not only about admiring the exquisiteness of the old objects, but also about making comparisons between the various eras. The various antiquities displayed by the exhibition have been carefully selected and organized, from ancient times to the present, and are systematically displayed according to their development strategies. Therefore, the origin of the establishment of various arts and the process of development can be known. This is truly a good opportunity for us to study the national culture. Not only artists, antiquarians, and teachers and students of various schools should go to visit, but ordinary people should also go to see it, so as to understand the situation of our national culture and cultivate a spirit of respecting art.

Overview of National Foreign Trade in the First Quarter of This Year: Exports Increased by More Than Six Million Yuan Compared to Last Year; Imports Decreased by More Than Thirty-three Million Yuan 104

According to the Xinxin News Agency, the situation of foreign trade in the first quarter of this year is much worse than that in the first quarter of last year. The total value of trade in the first quarter of this year is 389,818,000 yuan, which is a decrease of 26,754,000 yuan compared to 416,572,000 yuan in the same period last year. The Statistics Department of the International Trade Bureau has prepared a systematic report based on the customs records and with reference to the trade situation in the same period last year to provide a reference for those who care about international trade. The details are as follows:

Increase in Exports, Decrease in Trade Deficit: The total value of imports in the first quarter of this year was 254,000,386 yuan, a decrease of 33,645,426 yuan compared to the same period last year. The total value of exports was 235,818,505 yuan, an increase of 6,891,568 yuan compared to the same period last year. The trade deficit was 118,181,881 yuan, a decrease of 40,537,000 yuan compared to the same period last year. This is a slightly optimistic phenomenon.

Rice and Grain Imports Slightly Active: Among imported commodities, there was no significant change in the first quarter of this year compared to the same period last year. However, rice and grain imports were slightly active. This is because the drought last year resulted in insufficient domestic agricultural production to meet demand. All orders for foreign rice were successively imported in the spring of this year, so the figures increased compared to last year. It is estimated that the first quarter of this year was more than 16.6 million gold units, an increase of more than 9 million gold units compared to the same period last year. Even wheat flour increased compared to last year, reaching more than 1 million gold units in the first quarter of this year. However, wheat decreased by nearly 2 million gold units. In total, imports of miscellaneous grains in the first quarter of this year were 25,227,000 gold units, equivalent to more than 47 million national currency, an increase of more than 13 million yuan compared to the same period last year.

Sharp Decrease in Imports of Yarn, Cotton, and Cotton Goods: Imports of cotton yarn, cotton, etc. in the first quarter of this year were equivalent to more than 12 million yuan, a significant decline of more than 18 million yuan compared to the same period last year. Imports of cotton goods were equivalent to more than 6.52 million yuan, also a significant decrease compared to last year. Other items such as wood, metals, mineral sands, machinery, fish, seafood, and paper all increased, especially metals and mineral sands, which increased significantly. Sugar, vehicles, boats, metal products, tobacco, kerosene, diesel oil, etc. all tended to decline, with tobacco, kerosene, and diesel oil experiencing the largest declines.

Sharp Increase in Exports of Tung Oil and Peanuts: As for exported commodities, exports of raw silk in the first quarter of this year also declined, estimated at more than 5 million yuan, a decrease of more than 1 million yuan compared to the same period last year. The situation for tea was relatively good, estimated at more than 5.28 million yuan, a slight increase compared to the same period last year, but the amount was also small, only an increase of more than 160,000 yuan. Exports of egg products in the first quarter of this year were estimated at more than 3.9 million yuan, a decrease of more than 1 million yuan compared to the same period last year. The sluggish exports are due to the weak sales to England, because the main market for undifferentiated wet yellow and white egg whites is England. The situation for tung oil was better. In the first quarter of this year, it was estimated at more than 6.4 million yuan, an increase of more than 1.2 million yuan compared to the same period last year. Cotton was estimated at more than 3 million yuan, a decrease. Other exports such as vegetables, fish, beans, miscellaneous grains, fruits, and peanuts all increased, with peanut exports being even more robust, increasing threefold compared to the same period last year, which is slightly optimistic. Raw silk and leather goods all declined.

United States Ranks First Among Trading Countries: From the perspective of countries, in terms of imports, the United States still ranks first in the first quarter of this year, accounting for 19.90% of the total. It is followed by Japan, then by England, Germany, and Annam. In terms of exports, the United States also ranks first, followed by Hong Kong and Japan. The United States accounts for 24.6% of the total exports, a slight increase compared to the same period last year. Japan has declined slightly. As for the ports, Shanghai and Tianjin are both major trading ports in the north and south. Shanghai did not experience much increase or decrease in the first quarter, while Tianjin experienced a relatively large drop in exports.

Silk Merchant Zhu Zhongjia Kidnapped, Escapes Danger by Desperately Crying Out for Help, Kidnappers Brazenly Seize Him at His Doorstep and Drive Straight to Zhabei, Zhu Escapes After Being Thrown and Injured 105

At 9:15 PM the night before last, a major kidnapping case occurred inside the Old West Gate of the Nanshi district on Menghua Street. Fortunately, the victim desperately cried out for help, and the kidnappers, realizing they were in danger of being caught, threw him to the side of the road and fled in all directions, disappearing without a trace. The victim was fortunate to escape. The details are as follows:

Self-Built Residence: No. 79 Menghua Street inside the Old West Gate of the Nanshi district is the self-built residence of Zhu Zhongjia, a native of Dongting Mountain in Suzhou. Zhu is 47 years old. He previously ran a silk shop on Beijing Road for many years. Later, as the silk industry declined, he closed the shop. However, Zhu had some assets, so he built several shikumen-style houses on Menghua Street, naming the lane Jia Zhi Lane.

Criminals Covet: Zhu's self-built mansion, located at No. 79 along the road in the lane, was where his entire family lived. Unexpectedly, this attracted the covetous eyes of criminals. Around 9 PM the night before last, Zhu's wife, Yan, had gone to Suzhou and had not yet returned. Zhu, his brother Yousong, and several people with the surnames Zhou and Qin were chatting in the overpass building of their residence when suddenly five or six kidnappers broke in through the back door and went straight upstairs. As soon as they saw Zhu, they pulled out a handgun and monitored everyone's movements.

Kidnapping in Progress: At the same time, one of the kidnappers used Zhu's phone to hire a car from Yunfei Automobile Company on Fangbang Road, Ximen: Concession No. 12300, Chinese Area No. 4263. The driver was surnamed Lu. Once the car arrived at Zhu's house, two of the kidnappers dragged Zhu downstairs, forced him into the car, put a pair of black glasses on him, and ordered the driver to take the car to Yongxing Road in Zhabei.

Desperate Cry for Help: On the way, the driver, surnamed Lu, noticed that the men looked suspicious and unusual. Realizing something was wrong, he dared not speak out to avoid endangering himself. When the car arrived at the entrance of Maoying Dyeing Factory at No. 70 Yongxing Branch Road and stopped, the two kidnappers forced Zhu out of the car, planning to hide in their den on foot. Seeing this, Zhu desperately cried out that he was being kidnapped. The kidnappers, realizing their plan was failing, threw Zhu forcefully to the ground and fled in all directions.

Escorted to Nanshi: Zhu injured his foot in the fall and was unable to get up for a while. Fortunately, the driver, surnamed Lu, was alert and drove the car back, helped Zhu into the car, and reported to the Yongxing Road Police Station of the North Station Branch Bureau. The police chief, Chen Jiwu, briefly questioned Zhu. Since the case occurred within the jurisdiction of the Wenmiao Road Police Station in Nanshi, he ordered patrol officer Tong Boya to escort Zhu to the Wenmiao Road Police Station.

Medical Treatment: Police Chief Tang then questioned Zhu in detail and immediately reported to the headquarters, instructing all detective teams to pay attention to intercepting the kidnappers. Police Chief Tang also escorted Zhu Zhongjia to his home and called the famous bone-setting doctor Shi Xiaoshan for treatment. It was reported that a long period of recovery was required.

Excessive Quantity of Foreign Rice, 700,000 Bags Canceled with Foreign Firms, Buyers Were Small and Medium-Sized Rice Merchants in Northern and Southern Markets, Approximately One Million Bags of Foreign Rice Currently in Shanghai 106

Regarding the matter of rice merchants and banks in Shanghai and other ports ordering a total of over 6.2 million bags of foreign rice from Saigon, Siam, etc., 700,000 of these bags were ordered by small and medium-sized merchants. Fearing that an oversupply of foreign rice would lead to losses and impact the market, they canceled their contracts with the managing foreign firms. Details are as follows:

Total Quantity of Foreign Rice Arrived: After various provinces in China experienced floods and droughts last year, resulting in poor harvests, rice merchants and banks in Shanghai and other ports entrusted 17 foreign firms, including Heyi and Dalong, to order foreign rice from Saigon, Siam, and Xiaojiao, totaling over 6.2 million bags. These were shipped to Shanghai in batches, starting from October last year to April 20th of this year. The total quantity of foreign rice that arrived in Shanghai and Ningbo was approximately 5 million bags.

700,000 Bags Canceled: Among the over 6.2 million bags of foreign rice, 700,000 bags were ordered by small and medium-sized merchants in the northern and southern markets of Shanghai. After a large amount of foreign rice was imported into China, the government and various organizations paid great attention due to the impact on the rural economy. Furthermore, with fluctuating rice prices, rice merchants with smaller financial resources felt uneasy, fearing future losses and fundamental disruptions to their businesses. To maintain stability, they canceled contracts with the managing foreign firms last week, totaling over 700,000 bags. The rice merchants voluntarily compensated the foreign firms for breach of contract according to the original orders.

Quantity of Foreign Rice in Shanghai: Of the 5 million bags of foreign rice already shipped to Shanghai, 4 million bags have been sold inland. Currently, there are only about 1 million bags of foreign rice stored in Shanghai. However, there are over 1.2 million bags in various other locations. Now that 700,000 bags have been canceled, there are only 500,000 bags that have not yet been shipped from overseas.

Since the Pudong Gaoqiao Rural Improvement Association established a branch in Xilingjiazhai, it has been diligently working on village administration, sanitation, and education. In order to attract cocoon transport, the Railway Bureau, in the previous cocoon season, instructed the Traffic Department to assign dedicated personnel from various traffic departments to be responsible for reception. Now that the cocoon season is approaching again, the department has not only instructed various sections to broadly attract cocoon transport but also ordered them to follow the previous example, assigning personnel to each cocoon transport station within their respective sections to be specifically responsible for reception. Lixing Thermos Factory Expands Operations, New Factory Site Built 110

Thermos bottles are essential household items. In the past, imported goods flooded the market, resulting in an astonishing amount of annual leakage. Mr. Gan Dounan, a Ningbo merchant, was concerned about this and, in 1928, invested in establishing the Lixing Thermos Factory on Dongyouheng Road in Shanghai, specializing in the production of Great Wall brand thermos bottles. Immersed in diligent research and careful study, after several years of painstaking operation, the products reached more than 40 varieties. Known for their novel designs and accurate temperature retention, they are praised by society. Recently, Mr. Gan used his ingenuity to invent a rubber-wrapped mouth that tightly wraps the bottle mouth, preventing water seepage, completely solving the only major problem of rust water inside the thermos bottle. Mr. Gan's profound achievements can be seen from this. Recognizing that the supply of goods could not meet the demand, the factory found that its original location was insufficient for its operations. Therefore, it purchased land on Quanjia'an Road in Zhabei to build a state-of-the-art factory building, adopting scientific management in order to increase production. After several months of construction, it has recently been fully completed. The vast buildings are connected, and Mr. Gan's perseverance and knowledge are worthy of being a model for our industrial sector.

Cosmetics and New Pharmaceutical Industries Request Refund of Industrial Alcohol Tax, Will Join Five Industrial Groups to Proceed 114

Since the Ministry of Finance implemented a unified tax on alcohol, (ordinary tax of 13 cents per liter was changed to 6.5 cents per liter for modified alcohol) the cosmetics and new pharmaceutical industries, using alcohol as an essential industrial raw material, have seen increased costs after the unified tax was levied, indirectly fostering opportunities for foreign goods to be dumped on the market. Therefore, they have repeatedly submitted requests to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce and other organizations to be forwarded to the central government, requesting that the unified tax on alcohol used for industrial purposes be refunded. So far, no approval has been received. The Pharmaceutical Manufacturers Association has specially sent letters to the Municipal Society for the Promotion of National Goods, the China National Goods Maintenance Association, the National Goods Datong Alliance, the National Goods Factories Association, the Mechanized National Goods Factories Association, and other national goods organizations, scheduling a joint meeting to jointly request a tax refund.

Among them, there is a couplet by Li Bai, "Containing the ancient and modern knowledge, gathering the essence of the earth," with soaring brushstrokes and a harmonious atmosphere, and the paper, ink, and vermilion are all antique and elegant, which is rare to see. Recent News from the Isola Circus 116

Since the Isola Circus of England opened on the open space across from the Great World, it has been crowded with spectators every day, and the scene has been unprecedented in Shanghai. According to general opinion, the programs performed by the Isola Circus this week are very exciting, especially the "King of Heaven" and "Cuban Cossack Knights" acts. The so-called "King of Heaven" refers to aerial acrobats. Four performers climb onto the trapeze, flipping and soaring through the air, which is quite thrilling. The four Cuban knights are incomparably brave. They can somersault off the horse while the horse is galloping, or hook one foot on the horse's back and drag their hands on the ground. The audience applauded and exclaimed. When performing in Australia, an American circus offered a large sum of money to buy the actors of the above two acts, but all the actors loved Isola's character and never moved by the heavy interest. Respectable! In addition, in one of the scenes where lions and tigers performed together, the conductor was an Indian who entered the lion and tiger enclosure barehanded, with a stern look and a commanding voice. The audience was amazed. Also, this time, the Isola Grand Beast Garden has 300 kinds of rare birds and animals, which are open daily from 7 am, noon, and 9 pm to 5 pm. The entrance fee is 20 cents for adults and 10 cents for children. It is reported that the troupe owner, Isola, is kind and loving and will hold special performances for children, soldiers, and sailors in the future. It is currently being planned. There are currently two shows every day, a day show at 5 pm and a night show at 9:15 pm. The ticket prices are low, and children's tickets are only half price for the day show.

Pushan Hospital Examines Man Wounded by Ax, Murderer is Friend of the Deceased, Reason is Failure to Obtain Loan 117

On the afternoon of the 23rd of this month, at around 4 PM, Pushan Hospital on Xinmin Road in Zhabei received a man wounded by an ax, sent by police from the North Station Branch Bureau. At the time, the injured man was unable to speak. The person accompanying him said that the man's name was He Shanzeng, 33 years old, from Yixing, currently living in Zhongshan Lane on Zhongshan Road, etc. After the doctor's examination, it was found that He Shanzeng had been struck with an ax on his right temple and jaw, each about an inch deep. The blood vessels had been severed, and all the blood had drained out, so he died the next afternoon. However, the deceased was injured within the jurisdiction of the North Station Branch Bureau, but died at the hospital within the jurisdiction of the Xinzha Branch Bureau. Therefore, the hospital reported to the Xinzha Branch Bureau, which sent police to investigate. Chief Ruan of the branch ordered Lu Abin, the local security officer of the 11th district, to report to the Shanghai District Court for an autopsy yesterday morning. At 3:25 PM, Prosecutor Xiao Jinying arrived at the scene and found that the deceased, He Shanzeng, had indeed died from his injuries. He immediately filled out a burial certificate and ordered the security officer to arrange for the burial and wait for the arrest of the murderer. Later, the security officer investigated and summoned the deceased's family to the scene. They stated that the murderer who killed He Shanzeng was originally a friend of the deceased. He had previously borrowed money from He to open a shop, but the shop was never opened, and the money was used up. This time, he wanted to borrow money from He again, but was unsuccessful, which caused him to hold a grudge and commit this heinous act. The body was prepared by the deceased's family with a coffin for burial.

Lawsuit of a Movie Actress 118

Wang Huijuan, a movie actress of the Star Film Company, is originally from Tianjin, 25 years old, and lives with her old mother at No. 9, Lane 120, Fuli Road, French Concession. Recently, because the Shanghai Daily continuously published her life, actions, and current living conditions, Wang believes that the newspaper's records are mostly speculative and have the intention of slandering her reputation. Therefore, she hired lawyers Jin Xinmin and Jin Yumin to file a criminal complaint of defamation against the newspaper's editors and publishers, Yu Lansun and Dong Qimeng, in the First Special District Court. The complaint states that since entering the film industry, she has been clean and self-respecting, but the environment is limiting. She once felt weary of the world. The newspaper actually continuously recorded matters related to her weariness of the world on March 30, April 1, 2, and 4, using knowingly false facts as material for deliberate defamation. It also lists three points of false information recorded by the Shanghai Daily, stating that her personal reputation has been completely ruined, and the entire film industry has been disgraced. She requests that the defendants be summoned to court and punished according to law. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Ye Shengchao opened the court to hear the case. Neither the plaintiff nor the defendants were present in person. Defendant Yu Lansun sent a letter in advance to request the court to postpone the hearing and stated that there was no such person as Dong Qimeng in the newspaper. However, the plaintiff's lawyers claimed that Dong Qimeng was one of the investors in the newspaper, according to an investigation by the Municipal Party Department, and that Dong Qimeng was also listed in the registration application submitted by the newspaper. Lawyer Jin then elaborated on the prosecution's intention, stating that the various sections recorded by the newspaper were quite lewd and truly unbearable to read. Therefore, he specially presented the newspaper to the court for review. Judge Ye glanced at it briefly and instructed that the newspaper be kept on file and that the hearing be rescheduled.

Complaint of a Young Woman Forced into Prostitution 120

Jiang Weibao, a woman from Wuxi, 21 years old, is fairly pretty. She used to live in the countryside in her hometown. Her father, Jiang Yongjia, remarried after his wife passed away. His new wife was quite fierce, causing Jiang to be unwelcome by her stepmother. A woman named Wang Sanyuan, who knew Jiang Yongjia well, took advantage of the opportunity to introduce Jiang to Shanghai to find work. She brought the woman to Shanghai and lived at No. 35, Daqing Lane, Nanjing Road. This was around April of last year. In early May, Wang Sanyuan used threats and sweet words to deceive Jiang Weibao and force her into prostitution. She had no choice but to obey. From then on, she was no longer pure and became a victim. This lasted for about four months. Jiang suffered greatly and contracted venereal disease and leucorrhea. Her life was no different from hell. Therefore, on December 21st of last year, she seized the opportunity to escape and, with the help of a patron, was treated at the Southeast Medical Clinic. She has not fully recovered to this day. Now, Jiang has filed a complaint with the Criminal Division of the First Special District Court, accusing Wang Sanyuan of restricting her freedom. Yesterday afternoon, Presiding Judge Feng Shide opened Criminal Division 1 to hear the case. The summons for Wang Sanyuan was not delivered, so she did not appear in court. After Jiang reported the situation, Judge Feng decided to reschedule the hearing.

Scavenging Child Finds Bomb, Reports to Police Station, Further Investigation into its Origin 121

Around 12:00 pm on the 25th, a Jiangbei scavenging child, about 12 or 13 years old, found a steel bomb resembling a one-pound thermos bottle from an unknown location. He was examining it under the electric light in front of the five-story Western-style building of Dayifang, across from Ruifuli on Dongzilaihuo Street, French Concession. The bomb seemed quite heavy, with a copper button at one end. Passersby stopped to watch, saying that it was a shrapnel bomb and extremely dangerous. The child was very frightened when he heard this, so he put the bomb in the trash can in front of No. 19 and turned to leave. Later, a neighbor at that location ran to tell the patrolling police. The police arrived and checked the trash can and found that it was indeed a bomb. They then reported back to the police station and sent detectives to take the bomb back to the police station. In addition to disposing of it, they will also investigate the origin of the bomb for verification.

French Water and Electricity Company Robbery: Robbers Sentenced; Xu Defu Receives Harshest Sentence as a Repeat Offender; Yang and Qiu Ordered to Pay 4,000 Yuan in Compensation 125

Tu Jinsheng, a comprador for the French Water and Electricity Company, ordered Qin Rongsheng, an employee, to withdraw 20,000 yuan in cash on the morning of February 2 of this year and transport it by company car to the bank for deposit. However, as Qin stepped out of the company gate and onto the car, four armed robbers ambushed him and stole 4,000 yuan. Police Inspector General Jin Jiulin of the Special Task Force of the French Police, along with detectives Zhang Ziying, Qian Yumin, Qin Youyu, and officers Dai Rongji, Ma Yizhi, Wu Wengang, Xu Youyi, and Zhu Jutong, arrested the robbers and suspects Qiu Yanshou, Yang Yang, Li Zhongxin, Zhu Hanqiang, Zhang Yunpeng, Pan Yuqing, Liu Shugen, Zhang Debiao, Zhao Zhongheng, Fan Youheng, Xu Shugen, Pan Yibang, Zhou Kui, Zhou Lu (female), Xia Wenfu, Xu Yuecheng, and Xu Defu, seventeen men and women in total, on the 17th of last month at various locations including 25 Dafang Lane, Fangbang Bridge, 34 Derun Lane, Chezhan Road, 480 Fangxie Road, 27 Anshun Lane, Kangti Road, and Dafang Inn at 381 Avenue Edward VII. They also confiscated two Browning pistols and sixteen bullets, bringing them back to the police station to be handed over to the Second Special District Court for interrogation and detention. As a result, Qiu Yanshou, Yang Yang, Zhang Debiao, Fan Youheng, Liu Shugen, Zhao Zhongheng, Zhou Kui, Zhou Lu, and Xu Defu were publicly prosecuted on charges of robbery under Article 348 of the Criminal Code and Article 1 of the Regulations for the Suppression of Military Firearms. Among the remaining eight individuals, who were found to be unrelated after investigation, Pan Yibang was temporarily detained and transferred at the request of the Water Police, as he had committed robbery in the interior. The other seven were released without charge by the police. The French Water and Electricity Company also hired Attorney Ba He to represent them and filed a private lawsuit to recover the stolen 4,000 yuan. All this was reported in detail previously. Judge Zhang Chaozuo of the Second Special District Court held several hearings and appointed lawyers to defend the defendants, declaring the trial concluded. Yesterday, at 10:00 AM, Judge Zhang presided over the hearing in the First Criminal Division, ordering the defendants to be brought before the court. Yang Yang was sentenced to seven years imprisonment for armed robbery with more than three accomplices and two years imprisonment for possession of military firearms and bullets for criminal purposes, to be served concurrently for a total of nine years. Qiu Yanshou was sentenced to five years imprisonment for conspiring with more than three accomplices in robbery and two years imprisonment for receiving stolen goods, to be served concurrently for a total of six years. Xu Defu, as a repeat offender of continuous robbery, was sentenced to eleven years imprisonment. Zhao Zhongheng was sentenced to two years and six months imprisonment for buying and selling military firearms without permission and without proving legitimate reasons. Fan Youheng (same charges as Zhao) was sentenced to one year imprisonment. Zhou Kui (same charges) was sentenced to three months imprisonment. The number of days spent in pre-trial detention will be deducted from the sentence at a rate of two days for each day of imprisonment. The two pistols and sixteen bullets were confiscated. Yang Yang and Qiu Yanshou were jointly ordered to compensate the French Water and Electricity Company 4,000 yuan. Zhang Debiao, Liu Shugen, and Zhou Lu were found not guilty. All defendants were returned to the detention center pending appeal. Zhao Zhong'en and Zhang Debiao, who was found not guilty, were wanted by the Public Security Bureau for another robbery case in the Chinese area. The judge ordered them to be detained and transferred to face trial.

A warrant was obtained from the First Special District Court, and Xie Wenquan was summoned to the Second Criminal Division yesterday morning. Plaintiff Chen Guanyun stated that he married Jia Caili, a woman from Yangzhou, last August. After living together for only a few months, Wu absconded with all their belongings, emulating Hong Fu's elopement. After searching extensively without success, he reported the matter to the Sixth District Public Security Bureau in Caojiadu, which was approved. teahouse for a while. Soon, they saw his wife, Wu Caili, entering Mao's law office with the defendant, Xie Wenquan, hand in hand. They followed them inside. Once inside the office, he, the defendant, and Wu Caili went into a small room, while the others were not allowed to enter. The defendant took out a blank sheet of paper and asked him to sign it. After he signed, the defendant said that signing meant they were divorced. He refused. At that time, his wife tried to leave, and he tried to stop her. Lawyer Mao then slapped him and grabbed his collar, ordering the defendant Xie Wenquan

to tightly squeeze his scrotum. He cried out in pain, and the defendant released him and ran away. He chased after him and encountered a Chinese detective, and they all went to the police station. He is now accusing the defendant Xie Wenquan and Lawyer Mao Xianshen of joint assault. Witnesses Yan Lianqi and Wang Yongbao testified that they witnessed Chen being beaten. Wu Caili stated that she was eighteen years old and from Yangzhou. She had studied opera since childhood and sang in various restaurants and hotels. Last August, Chen Guanyun forcibly married her, compelling her to live with him. Unable to bear the abuse, she left in September and now lives with her mother, Wu Xu, at 181 Hengtong Road, Zhabei. She commissioned Lawyer Mao to write

a letter to Chen requesting a divorce. On that day, she went to Lawyer Mao's office, and Chen grabbed her, trying to pull her back. She refused, leading to a conflict, but there was no beating. Xie Wenquan denied the assault. Lawyer Mao Xianshen testified that Chen and Wu Caili did argue that day. Chen insisted on taking Wu away, but Wu refused. He tried to mediate and forbade them from arguing in the office. Chen

was aggressive and refused to listen. He then called the police. There was no fighting. Wu Caili's mother, Wu Xu, testified that her daughter was forcibly taken away by Chen to live with him. Chen is an unemployed rogue who specializes in extortion. Five years ago, he injured his own leg in a case involving a woman and extorted hundreds of yuan. Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Instructs on Appealing Stamp Tax Assessments; Appeals Should Be Filed Within Five Days of Judgment 132

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce issued a statement saying that the city has been very strict lately regarding stamp tax inspections. According to current regulations, after an inspection, the case should be sent to the court for trial. After being inspected and before the court hearing, all stores should review their seized books and records to determine whether stamps are required and whether they are sufficient, according to the current stamp tax regulations. They can consult with their respective trade associations or request instructions from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to present during the hearing. If they disagree with the court's judgment, they should file an appeal with the competent higher court within five days of receiving the ruling, according to the Ministry's regulations. Following the example of requesting the trade association to request the Chamber of Commerce to forward a letter for exemption will not only be unhelpful but will also miss the statutory appeal deadline.

Sweetheart Candy Wrapper Case Verdict 135

The American merchant company, Haining & Co., previously discovered that Jin Yuehan, who opened the Huierkang Candy Store at Fukangli, Daxi Road, Jing'an Temple Road in this port, had counterfeited the trademark of the company's Sweetheart Candy wrapper. It filed a lawsuit with the District Court for investigation. It has been learned that the case has been concluded, with a verdict stating that the defendant's actions warrant a sentence of two months imprisonment under Article 268 of the Illegal Acts Law. However, considering that the defendant had only recently taken over Xu Linsen's business for a short time, that he had changed the candy wrapper after receiving notice from Haining & Co., and that he has not been sentenced to penal servitude or a higher penalty, it is in compliance with the conditions for a suspended sentence under Article 90, Paragraph 1 of the same law. Therefore, according to Article 315 of the Criminal Procedure Law, the verdict is as stated in the main text, with a two-year suspended sentence.

Mr. Chen Zuogan, the manager of the Lianhua Woolen Mill on North Henan Road in this city, has a keen eye for social psychology. Several years ago, he created dozens of kinds of domestic swimwear and sportswear to meet the needs of all sectors. Since its inception, it has been very popular. Due to the New Life Movement, swimming is listed as one of the compulsory sports, and the successful production of dehydrated wool has led to an overwhelming number of orders for the factory's Sanlun Shuanglun swimwear from various ports, creating a situation where they are struggling to keep up with demand. Recently, the factory has also created a new type of pure silk men's short socks, which are manufactured using scientific methods and chemical dyeing. The production rate is very rapid. Statistics show that the consumption rate of these socks is the highest among Westerners, especially sailors from various countries who buy them back home to give to relatives and friends. Due to the excessive number of swimwear orders, the factory is working around the clock to increase production, with employees working in shifts. The factory's efforts in production and quality improvement are commendable and can help reverse some of China's import surplus of foreign goods.

Business Report of Bank of Communications 144

Introduction

Another year has passed since the last general meeting of shareholders. During this past year, the domestic economy has become increasingly difficult, and it has been difficult to advance the bank's business, and it has not been possible to retreat. At a crossroads, there is no place to stand. Therefore, after repeated deliberation, we can only strive to fulfill the bank's mission of developing industry. On the one hand, we will improve internal work and increase efficiency, and on the other hand, we will cooperate with all parties to seek adjustments. Regarding the expansion of the business network, there are the establishment of branches in coastal ports and the upper and lower reaches of the Yangtze River, as well as the establishment of agricultural warehouses. The area from Qinzhong to Jin Sui in the northwest is also an area to be developed. All measures are aimed at assisting the rural economy and regulating commercial finance. Although the times are difficult and there are many thorny issues, we will find a corresponding way out by adhering to the direction and opening up paths. The following is a summary of the domestic and foreign economic situation, a brief description of the bank's progress, and the future direction of our efforts. Please examine them carefully.

(1) Situation in the Domestic and Foreign Economic Circles

In recent years, the domestic economy has been extremely depressed, and financial business has also become increasingly tight. The internal reasons for this are due to the invasion of major disasters and human misfortunes and the imperfect management methods, while the external reasons are due to the pressure of the international economy, that is, the prevailing inflation in various countries and the role of controlled economy. Almost none of them are not related to the interests of China's economic undertakings, and none of them are not related to the gains and losses of financial business. Therefore, none of the phenomena are not contrary to the form of the domestic economic society. As a result, financial undertakings based on the economic society can only increase difficulties and cannot coordinate. Internally, they are troubled by the decline of industry and commerce, and externally, they are affected by the pressure of the international economy. The seriousness of the problem can be seen in general. Now, to explore the external reasons, let us first examine the situation in the domestic and foreign economic circles for comparison. (To be continued)
