Review of Ten Lectures on Chinese Philosophy 146

— Chen Gaoyong

Written by Li Shicen, published by World Book Company, priced at two yuan

This is a collection of lectures by Mr. Shi Cen before his death, which was recently published after his death. The content includes: a comparative study of Chinese philosophy and Western philosophy, the Confucian view of logic, the Mohist theory of Shangtong and its practical spirit, the Taoist view of the universe, the nominalist concept of dialectics and formal logic, the philosophy of the Doctrine of the Mean, what is Neo-Confucianism, the theory of the unity of body and use, the philosophy of life, and other ten articles. Among the ten articles, the first article, "Comparative Study of Chinese Philosophy and Western Philosophy," can be said to be a general article, and it can also be said to be his methodology for lecturing on Chinese philosophy. Therefore, we only need to read this article to know what attitude he takes to understand Chinese philosophy, and we can also know whether his understanding of Chinese philosophy is accurate.

When Mr. Li was alive, he often thought that his philosophical views had changed, from idealism to materialism, and it was still "new materialism," that is, dialectical materialism. However, we have not seen any new methods or insights from the articles and books he published until his death. Moreover, because of the fixed views of idealism for many years, suddenly adding a few so-called "new materialism" phrases and terms can be considered a bit of "drawing a tiger and failing to resemble it." This "Ten Lectures on Chinese Philosophy" seems to represent his more thorough views after the transformation. Therefore, if we only look at his personal articles and books, this book can be said to be "Li Shicen's works," because so-called works should at least be based on a "consistent method" and be able to "explain" the things being lectured on. If only a lot of facts and theories are arranged and described, then it can only be said to be "compilation and narration," and it is not enough to speak of works. Therefore, we say that if we look at the books published by Li Shicen personally, his "Philosophy of Life" and "Introduction to Philosophy" can only be said to be "compilation and narration," and only this book can be said to be his "works." However, if we look at it from the perspective of real works, whether this book is qualified to be a work is another question.

The content of this book is entirely based on the method of comparison between Chinese and Western cultures. Therefore, he compares Confucius with Socrates, Mencius with Plato, Xunzi with Aristotle, Zhuang Lao with Heraclitus, Zhu Hui'an, Wang Yangming with Aquinas, Scotus, and compares Song and Ming Neo-Confucianism with scholastic philosophy. He compared Wang Chuanshan, Yan Xizhai, and Dai Dongyuan with Kant, Schopenhauer, and Nietzsche, and so on, there is no need to list them all. This comparative method can indeed give readers a lot of inspiration, but the disadvantages of forced association also arise from this. We know that "analogy" is the simplest and easiest method to make mistakes in logic. Therefore, it cannot be used casually unless it is under extremely strict conditions and only when it is absolutely necessary. Religious people are best at using this method to preach, and idealists are also best at using this method to talk about metaphysics. Mr. Li lectured on Chinese philosophy and compared it with Western philosophy everywhere. Although it is more brilliant than religious people and metaphysicians using metaphors to preach and lecture, it still fails to transcend the extremely simple and easy-to-err "analogy." In other words, he ultimately failed to analyze and explain the facts and theories themselves so that people could grasp a clear concept. For example, he compared Zhu Hui'an, Wang Yangming with Aquinas, and Scotus, saying: "It can be seen that their hypocritical minds are the same." (Page 22) He also said: "Wang Yangming is an extreme idealist. He feels that Zhu Hui'an's idealism is not enough." (Page 337) We don't care whether Zhu Hui'an, Wang Yangming, Aquinas, and Scotus are the same, that is, in terms of Wang Yangming and Zhu Hui'an, why can the two factions be opposed? Isn't this a huge question that people who lecture on Chinese philosophy should quickly explain to us? However, Mr. Li only used the sentence "He felt that Zhu Hui'an's idealism was not enough" to perfunctorily deal with it. If so, why "lecture?" Of course, Mr. Li explained the reasons for the occurrence of Neo-Confucianism, saying: "The rich get richer, and the poor get poorer... This is also the "cause" that promoted Chinese philosophy to extreme idealism." (Page 286) It seems that he has explained it a bit, but when we think that in today's world, the rich get richer and the poor get poorer, but there is a prevalence of materialist philosophy, we feel that Mr. Li's explanation is still inexplicable.

Mr. Li also knows! "From the formal point of view, Chinese philosophy and Western philosophy do have many similarities, but when it comes to substance, there are many differences (page 27). But after reading the whole book, we only see him comparing the two from time to time, but we have not seen him being able to clearly explain the essence of Chinese philosophy. Then, the so-called "observing from the dialectical point of view," "observing from the materialist point of view," "observing from the dialectical materialist point of view" (see the first lecture) are just a set of fashionable decorations.

Although, this book is still the best book among Li's books. Mr. Li is dead. Those who want to read Mr. Li's works can buy it and read it.

Reading "The Philosophy of Life" 147

— Zhou Yuying

Published by Zhengzhong Bookstore, priced at six cents

Generally, people who study philosophy admit that the development of human spiritual knowledge can be divided into three stages, namely: (1) dogmatic, (2) skeptical, and (3) critical. But if we link the epistemology and ontology of philosophy together and observe them together, then the development of the ontology of philosophy can also be divided into three stages, namely: (1) theism, (2) from idealism to materialism, and (3) from empiricism to the philosophy of life.

Originally, when we study philosophy, epistemology and ontology cannot be mechanically separated. Although some scholars often only care about one and forget the other when discussing, forgetting epistemology when discussing ontology, and forgetting ontology when discussing epistemology, in fact, the connection between epistemology and ontology will never be severed by scholars' neglect and forgetfulness. In fact, the development of the ontology of philosophy itself develops with the development of human spiritual knowledge. For example, in the period when human knowledge is dogmatic and arbitrary, the explanation of all natural phenomena and human behaviors is only the responsibility of God. God is the most dogmatic and arbitrary thing, and God can be said to be the ontology of religious philosophy.

Dogmatic and arbitrary knowledge is shaken in the end, because God cannot explain everything in the universe, and the existence of God is also shaken. At this time, dogmatic knowledge and the theistic ontology collapse at the same time, and we enter the skeptical epistemology and the idealistic and materialistic ontology: in this period, mankind is liberated from the prison of God, and everything must be doubted, and the universe is loved and explained. Therefore, idealism and materialism are born from this skeptical epistemology. Idealism and materialism are born from skeptical epistemology, but later, when the systems of idealism and materialism are determined, the mind and matter also become "God," and the color of doubt is reduced or even eliminated.

However, whether it is idealism or materialism, they still cannot shoulder the responsibility of explaining natural phenomena and human behavior. Therefore, human skeptical knowledge has to move towards critical knowledge. With the progress of epistemology, the ontology will naturally progress with it. In the process of critical epistemology, mankind produced science. First, there was natural science, and then there was social science. Various departments of science were used to make analytical explanations of natural phenomena and human behavior. The remaining task of philosophy was to make comprehensive explanations. Therefore, the so-called idealism and materialism had to retreat and disappear in front of science. "Materialism? Where is matter! Idealism? The mind is about to die!" In this critical scientific world, Mr. Chen Lifu's sigh is really not accidental.

Human knowledge has entered the critical stage, and idealistic philosophy and materialistic philosophy can no longer exist. Therefore, empiricism and philosophies similar to empiricism have emerged like mushrooms after a rain. Empiricist philosophy still carries a strong color of skepticism in terms of epistemology, at most it is close to criticism. At the same time, in terms of ontology, some people say that it is a dualistic philosophy. In fact, we might as well say that it is an elementless philosophy. The empiricist philosophy, precisely because it is an elementless philosophy, its very existence is suspended and has nowhere to go. As a result, it can only be trapped in skepticism forever and cannot progress to correct criticism. Only the philosophy of life can accept the spirit of critical criticism correctly. "Life is the center of the universe, and people's livelihood is the center of human history." Mr. Sun Yat-sen determined the ontology of his philosophy in this way. At the same time, in terms of past philosophy, "one God" is really just a symbol of life, and the so-called "mind and matter are one" is really just two sides of life. From the side of life, it is the mind, and from the other side, it is matter. There is absolutely no isolated mind in the world, nor is there an isolated matter. However, idealists and materialists insist on pulling half of their bodies to isolate them. If history could speak, it would really cry out loudly!

The publication of Mr. Chen Lifu's "Philosophy of Life" not only consolidated the theoretical foundation of the Chinese revolution. After its system is completely established, I believe it will also make the greatest contribution to world philosophy? However, the reporter cannot help but regret that "The Philosophy of Life" has only published the first volume, and in this first volume, the system of explanation is not very clear. It is very difficult to read, and this has to require the original author to seek remedy as soon as possible.

Submission Guidelines for This Publication 148

1. This publication is a weekly publication, scheduled to be published every Saturday.

2. The purpose of this publication is to make a modest effort to "research," "introduce," and "criticize" the backward and poor academic and publishing circles in China with a serious attitude.

3. This publication welcomes external contributions on the following items: (a) Personal reading experience, (b) Research on Chinese and foreign writers, (c) Summary of famous Chinese and foreign works, (d) Introduction and criticism of books and newspapers, (e) News from cultural circles in various places.

4. We especially welcome painting drafts and woodcuts related to reading and the publishing industry.

5. The number of words in the manuscript should preferably be within 2,000 words.

6. Please indicate your name and mailing address in the manuscript.

7. All manuscripts will not be returned regardless of whether they are published or not. However, this does not apply to those with a return envelope and sufficient postage.

8. Once the manuscript is published, a small remuneration of 2 yuan to 4 yuan per thousand words will be paid.

9. Please send the manuscript to 234 Aimeiyu Xian Road, Shanghai.

Shanghai International Games Standing Committee Agrees on Specific Regulations 151

The Standing Committee of this year's International Track and Field Games held a meeting at the Naval YMCA at 5:30 PM on the 24th. Those present were Hall Swina (US), McKenna Madi (UK), Agasti (France), Stanav (Russia), Pike (Germany), and Zhou Jiaji (China). Hall was elected chairman, and Zhou Jiaqi recorded the minutes. The following matters were resolved: (1) The minimum number of participants from each country is one, which can be called a unit; (2) The maximum number of participants from each country in each event is four, plus two alternates; (3) The staff of the Games will be determined by the Standing Committee members at the next meeting; (4) Except for the bamboo pole for pole vaulting, all other sports equipment will be prepared by the Association; (5) The next Standing Committee meeting is scheduled for 5:30 PM on May 1st at the Naval YMCA; (6) The Public Security Bureau is requested to maintain order on the field, with the assistance of military police from participating countries; (7) A press box is set up for news reporters, who are not allowed to enter the competition field; (8) Participants must report to the athletes' changing room; (9) The Innes Military Band cannot participate; the McCrae Military Band will come to the field to play music, increasing interest; (10) A separate grandstand is set up for athletes. By a Difference of Two Points, Central Loses to Xie Xing, Result 39 to 37, Central Team Departs for Suzhou Today 154

After the Central Party Headquarters basketball team came to Shanghai, it won four and lost one. Yesterday's match against Xie Xing was the team's last battle in Shanghai. It was held at the Shen Garden basketball court at 6 PM. It is learned that Xie Xing is organized by the Xie Xing Sports Equipment Company, mainly composed of the Fudan University team, and Pan Chengbin of Dongya Sports College was also invited to join. Their strength is very strong. The competition between the two teams was fierce and the performance was spectacular. As a result, Xie Xing defeated Central by a difference of 39 to 37, two points.

Tie After the start, Tian Kang of Central opened the scoring with a free throw. Unexpectedly, Zhou Dayun of Xie Xing scored four consecutive goals in an instant, and the momentum was great. Central immediately adopted a delaying tactic to temporarily avoid the edge. Liu Daguan worked harder with his elusive appearances, and Tian Kang, not willing to lag behind, immediately caught up. Sure enough, he succeeded in scoring ten points quickly and took the lead with 11 to 10, one point ahead. After Qiu Guangxie of Xie Xing returned a goal, Tian Kang of Central added two points again, still taking the lead with 13 to 12. Zhou Dayun's free throw tied the score at 13 to 13.

Leading Thereafter, Central only had the power to follow, and Xie Xing led the way. However, the difference was only two or three points. Zhou Dayun of Xie Xing made the most contributions, while Central relied on the achievements of Tian and Liu. The defense of both sides was very impressive. At the end of the first half, Xie Xing had 25 points and Central had 19 points. In the second half, Xie Xing used three substitutes. At the beginning, the situation was still very prosperous. After a long stalemate, Chuan Ruixiang quickly scored two goals, and Han and Zhang each made contributions. Liu and Tian of Central lost momentum, and Jin Fei rose up, scoring three consecutive goals. Liu Daguan added two points again, restoring the original state, making it 33 to 27, still 6 points behind Xie Xing.

Pressing Although Xie Xing replaced the official personnel one after another, they ultimately relied on the three reserve troops as the main force, so their vigor was difficult to maintain for a long time. Central was pressing hard, step by step. Liu Daguan performed the best, while Tian Kang scored the most points. The scores were repeatedly chased up. Xie Xing was trapped in defense and could not use it. The situation became more and more tense. Finally, Central relied on one throw and one free throw from Liu and Tian, creating 37 to 39, with a difference of only two points. It is a pity that there was no more time, and Central lost to Xie Xing by a difference of two points. Referee: Dai Changlin. The results are as follows:

Jiaxing Teachers Went on Strike Yesterday, Primary and Secondary School Education Fees Are Nine Months in Arrears 167

(Jiaxing, 26th Dispatch) The county-run primary and secondary school education fees in the entire county have been in arrears for nine months. The principals of various schools have repeatedly petitioned, but the authorities have not been able to cope with the situation. From the morning of the 26th, the teachers of various schools unanimously submitted their resignations and went on strike. They also telegraphed the provincial authorities for relief and distributed a declaration, asking for assistance from all walks of life. County Magistrate Wang, who is in training in Hangzhou, has been telegraphed by the county government to report everything and ask for instructions. In the afternoon, many student representatives petitioned the county, requesting an immediate solution so that their studies would not be interrupted. There was no solution by evening.

Secondary School Normal Education Research Association Held a Meeting of the Funding and Equipment Group Yesterday, Discussing Funding and Equipment Issues in Detail, Graduation Examination Meeting to Be Held Next Monday 170

The Funding and Equipment Group of the Secondary School Normal Education Research Association of this city held its first meeting at the YMCA of Eight Immortals Bridge at 2:00 PM yesterday. The Graduation Examination Group will hold its second meeting next Monday. The details are as follows:

Funding and Equipment Group Ni Wenya, Ba Jixuan, Cui Jianwu, Yan Zhenyu, Qi Zhengcheng, Xu Suwanzhong, Zhang Shilin, Lu Songqian, Association Shengdian from the Education Bureau, and Qian Fugong attended. Research issues: (1) How should the equipment of natural sciences in middle schools and normal schools be improved? The discussion results: A. Please ask the Ministry of Education to order the education departments of all provinces and cities to subsidize private schools with at least 40% of their funds each year for the purchase of natural science equipment for a period of three years starting from the 24th year of the Republic of China. B. Teachers of science subjects in each school should make full use of natural materials and make instruments and specimens by themselves within the possible range. C. The equipment of natural sciences in each school should pay attention to production education. D. The education departments of all provinces and cities should set up public science experiment halls. (2) Opinions on equipment standards and what percentage of school funding should be occupied by equipment funding for teaching? After discussion, A. It seems that Articles 43 and 44 of the Middle School Regulations are too general. A minimum equipment standard should be set. B. Article 44 of the Middle School Regulations should be determined by each school for 12 staff members working in the same room. (3) Opinions on the funding standards of the Ministry of Education? After discussion, it was believed that the funding allocation could be handled in accordance with the regulations of the Ministry of Education, but 5% of the total amount could be withdrawn from the equipment expenses as reserve funds. However, the use of this equipment fund must be submitted to the provincial and municipal education departments for approval. (4) How to reform the forgery of bills and the bad habits of stores, so that money can be returned to the public? After discussion, A. The accountant and the general affairs should not be handled by one person. B. Vigorously implement the school funding disclosure method. C. Purchases of more than 50 yuan should be passed by the affairs committee. D. Use the bidding method as much as possible within the possible range.

Graduation Examination Group The second research meeting of the Graduation Examination Group is scheduled to be held next Monday (April 29) at 2:00 PM. The research issues are (1) Should the calculation and disclosure methods of the examination results of the school be changed? (2) Several issues such as members proposing the abolition of graduation examinations. The chairman is still Chen Jicheng.

(1) Graduation Examination Group, April 29th at 2:00 PM. (2) Moral Education Military Group, April 30th at 2:00 PM. (3) Curriculum Teaching Group, May 1st at 3:00 PM. (4) Teacher Training Group, May 2nd at 3:00 PM. (5) Funding Equipment Group, May 3rd at 2:00 PM. All members of each group should attend on time. Science Lecture Competition Methods for All Levels of Schools in This City: City Education Bureau Formulates and Announces Three Types 174

The Shanghai Education Bureau issued an order to its affiliated schools at all levels, stating: "The Ministry of Education's order Gao Zong Yi Er No. 02272 stated: 'According to the report from the China Scientific Movement Association, scientific knowledge is closely related to national economy and people's livelihood, and the level of scientific knowledge among the general public in our country is particularly low. Fortunately, thanks to your ministry's painstaking efforts, science education in schools at all levels has gradually been brought on track in recent years. Considering the current situation, with rural areas bankrupt and the national situation in peril, teachers and students in schools can still study diligently. The knowledge of teachers and students is cultivated by the blood and sweat of their fathers and brothers and the nation. How can they turn a blind eye to the poverty of the people and the weakness of the nation? Furthermore, if the lives of the Chinese people are not scientificized and production is not changed, the general public will lose their ability to participate in the work of solving national crises and reviving the nation. In the current difficult times, school faculty and students should use their scientific knowledge in their spare time to popularize it among the public, so that schools and society are closely related, and people's lives can be improved. Our association is concerned about this and has spared no effort in promoting the scientificization of Chinese society from the beginning. However, due to our limited resources, it is difficult to achieve significant results. Now that the spring semester is beginning, we propose to order all levels of schools across the country to hold at least one public science lecture per month. Primary and secondary schools must also hold science lecture competitions every semester, and welcome the general public to attend, in order to improve the scientific knowledge of the public.' Upon receipt of the ministry's notification, which stated that 'the association's request is feasible and should be followed,' this bureau will formulate the 'Methods for Holding Public Science Lectures in Schools at All Levels in Shanghai' and the 'Methods for Holding Science Lecture Competitions in Primary and Secondary Schools in Shanghai,' so that the schools can follow them. In order to increase the interest of primary and secondary school students in science lectures, we have also formulated the 'Methods for the Shanghai Science Lecture Competition for Primary and Secondary Schools' as a basis for holding citywide competitions in the future. In addition to reporting to the Ministry of Education for record-keeping, we will announce the formulated methods in advance so that all schools are aware of them and implement them accordingly, reporting back for review. Do not neglect this matter.'"

Methods for the Shanghai Science Lecture Competition for Primary and Secondary Schools: (1) The Shanghai Education Bureau (hereinafter referred to as "this bureau") is holding a citywide science lecture competition for primary and secondary school students to improve students' scientific knowledge and lecture skills, named the "Shanghai Science Lecture Competition for Primary and Secondary Schools." (2) The Shanghai Science Lecture Competition for Primary and Secondary Schools will be held once per semester, with the date determined and announced by this bureau. (3) The competition is divided into two groups: middle school and elementary school. (4) All municipal and private middle schools in this city that have been registered should send one representative from both junior and senior high school to participate in the middle school group competition. (5) All municipal and private elementary schools in this city that have been registered should send one representative to participate in the elementary school group competition. (6) The representatives selected by each school to participate in the competition should, in principle, be the winning students from the school's science lecture competition. (7) Science lecture competitions may be divided into preliminary, semi-final, and final rounds if necessary. The location will be announced by this bureau. (8) The judges for the science lecture competition will be hired by this bureau. The judging criteria will be formulated and announced by this bureau. (9) Winners of the science lecture competition will be awarded prizes by this bureau. (10) These methods will take effect from the date of promulgation.

Methods for Holding Public Science Lectures in Schools at All Levels in Shanghai: 1. Schools at all levels in Shanghai shall hold at least one public science lecture per month, and shall implement it in accordance with these methods. 2. One week before holding a public science lecture, each school shall report the date, time, lecturer's name, and lecture materials to the City Education Bureau for public announcement, so that people from all walks of life can attend. 3. The lecturers for science lectures shall, in principle, be faculty members and students of the respective schools, but external lecturers may also be hired if necessary. 4. The location of the science lectures shall, in principle, be at the respective schools, but other public places may also be used if necessary. 5. The time of the science lectures shall be such as not to hinder studies and to facilitate attendance by people from all walks of life. 6. After each lecture, schools at all levels shall report the details of the event to the City Education Bureau for record within one week. 7. No fees shall be charged for the public to attend the lectures. 8. The expenses required for the lectures shall be paid from the school's regular expenses. 9. The methods for the public to enter the venue to attend the lectures shall be reported to the City Education Bureau for approval in advance, in accordance with the school's circumstances. 10. A person (the number of people shall be determined by each school according to actual needs) shall be responsible for hosting the science lectures and shall be reported to the City Education Bureau for record. 11. These methods shall take effect from the date of promulgation by the Shanghai Education Bureau.

Methods for Holding Science Lecture Competitions in Primary and Secondary Schools in Shanghai: 1. All primary and secondary schools in Shanghai (middle schools include senior high schools, junior high schools, and schools of equivalent level, and elementary schools are limited to senior grades) shall hold at least one science lecture competition per semester, and shall implement it in accordance with these methods. 2. One week before holding a competition, each school shall report the date, time, topic, and name of the speaker to the City Education Bureau for public announcement, so that people from all walks of life can attend, and the City Education Bureau will send personnel to observe. 3. Science lecture competitions in each school shall, in principle, be graded competitions. The number of representatives pre-selected at each level shall be determined by each school. 4. The location of the science lecture competition shall, in principle, be at the respective school, but other public places may also be used if necessary. 5. The time of the science lecture competition shall be such as not to hinder studies and to facilitate attendance by people from all walks of life. 6. The judges for the science lecture competition shall be hired by each school, and shall, in principle, be faculty members of the school, but may also be changed appropriately if necessary. 7. The judging criteria and reward methods for the science lecture competition shall be determined by each school. 8. The winning students in the science lecture competition of each school shall be designated as participants in the citywide competition. The methods for the citywide competition will be determined separately. 9. No fees shall be charged for the public to attend the lectures. 10. Within one week after holding a competition, each school shall report the details of the event to the City Education Bureau for record. 11. The methods for the public to enter the venue to attend the lectures shall be reported to the City Education Bureau for approval in advance, in accordance with the school's circumstances. 12. The expenses for holding the science lecture competition in each school shall be paid from the regular expenses. 13. Other implementation details of the competition shall be determined by each school. 14. These methods shall take effect from the date of promulgation.

Spring and Autumn, Special Edition on Strange Surnames

Let's Also Talk About Strange Surnames 177

— (Qian Nantie)

Reading the record of strange surnames in "Spring and Autumn" these days, I can't help but feel itchy to write. I have also made some records of rare surnames. My humble work, "Liyuanlou Collection," has a volume attached called "Research on Rare Surnames," which lists hundreds of surnames. Due to space limitations, I will not list them all here. Recently, I have gained some more knowledge, and I will list a few. I wonder if you can add some more?

In the list of successful candidates in the Qing Dynasty, there is "Lü" Luanju in the Shunzhi period, "Mi" Xiangzhen in the Yongzheng period, "Nian" Kesheng in the Qianlong period, and "Li" Jun and "Shui" Junshao in the Guangxu period. These are probably also in the category of strange surnames. In my hometown of Changshu, there is the double surname "Yin Li." Yin Liyao, a scholar of the Guangxu period, rose from a censor to the salt and tea commissioner of Sichuan. In Guangxi, there is "Pan" Zhuqi, who once served as the director of a provincial department. It is said that the Pan surname is descended from Panhu, but I don't know if it is true.

In Jiangyin, there are six surnames that are descendants of Fang Xiaoru. Currently, there is "Liu" Weizhao, who works as a teacher at Zhejiang Provincial Middle School. The director of the Shanghai Star Film Company used to be "Ma Xu" Weibang. Also, the "Pu Xuefeng" mentioned by Mr. Liu is from Changshu. "Pu Xue" is a double surname. As for the Pu surname, it is common everywhere and not strange. I am just correcting this.

Three Strange Surnames 178

— Zhou Zongheng

In the "Juwu Ji" written by Wei Yuan of the Qing Dynasty, there is a name "Dou Bin" because he wanted to prove that the saying "In the Guandong region, the people produce prime ministers; in the Guanxi region, the people produce generals" in the Book of Han was correct, so he cited many Qing Dynasty military generals from Shaanxi and Gansu. The note below says he was from Guyuan. Although the official position was not noted, the existence of this military general in the Qing Dynasty is probably verifiable. His surname can also be considered a strange surname.

Li: There were two people named Li in the early Qing Dynasty. One was Li Hanshi, and Wang Yuyang's poem "Three Worthies of Sūmén" contains the line: "Li Hanshi of Xihua, willingly poor as a scholar, serves his mother in a grass hut, fearing disgrace if he returns clean." It is singing about him. His original name was He and he was from Xihua. He was a licentiate of the Ming Dynasty. Because he was ashamed to share the same surname with the rebel Li Zicheng, he changed it to Li. The other was Li Hongchu, with the courtesy name Jiqi, from Xinghua County, Yangzhou. After the fall of the Ming Dynasty, he called himself the retired monk of Mount Heng. He can also be considered a patriot of the late Ming Dynasty. He also originally had the surname Li. The reason for his surname Li is that after the Incident of Jia Shen, he wrote to his son: "Our first ancestor Jiu, was a Li official, and his descendants were named Li. Later, due to similar pronunciation, they were also named Li. Now that the late emperor died for the country and the thief is named Li, how can I bear to share the same surname with the thief? My descendants should restore the surname Li." (See Ji Qiting Collection) The two of them were "known as the two Li's in the world" at the time. Today, we record this not only because their surnames are strange, but also because their strange surnames contain patriotic elements. We especially promote this to shame those who betrayed the country.

Guo: Ten years ago, I knew a friend named Guo Aikui. He was from Yantai and also liked to write, but I haven't seen any of his writings in a long time. I don't know what his situation is like. I feel that his surname seems to be very rare.

Let's Talk About Surnames Again 179

Autumn Child

Recently, there have been many articles about surnames in the Spring and Autumn, which shows that studying surnames is also a very interesting thing. How can those gentlemen who advocate "abolishing surname boundaries" be compared? However, our China is so big, and the population is so large. Looking at history, there were originally more than a hundred surnames among the ancients: the "Hundred Family Surnames" in elementary school textbooks only selected some of the more common hundred. As for whether surnames are strange or not, in my personal view, there is no absolute standard. Because you think it's strange, I don't think it's a surname. I think it's strange, and he doesn't think it's strange. A surname that is rare in this place is considered very strange, but in another place it is very common and not strange. The ancient saying "less seen, more strange" is more logical! I'm going to talk about some rare surnames again. Do readers think they are very strange? Or are they "Meh, nothing special"?

Dian Keming, from Wugong, Shaanxi, was a student in the first infantry class of the Whampoa Military Academy. Gan: Gan Cheng, with the style name Zuxun, from Zhejiang, was in the third infantry class of the military academy. Also, the engineering student Ge Minghou was from Gaoxian, Sichuan, and the division clerk Qie Sidian, with the style name Lianwu, was from Dayi, Sichuan, and Liu Qun, with the style name Xiaojun, was from Lishui County, Zhejiang. Xian Chixian, from Bazhong, Sichuan, was in the fifth infantry class, and Shou Lianbo, from Chenzhou, Hunan. The economics student Bian Zhenye, with the style name Weiru, was from Yongfeng, Jiangxi. The political science student Lu Yiceng was from Zhejiang, and Xuan Guanyi, with the style name Feng, was from Longmen, Guangdong. Qing Gui, with the style name Fangzhou, was from Wugang, Hunan, and Yan Lianggui, with the style name Lanshan, was also from Hunan. Man: There are two workers, Man Yunchen and Man Shiming, in the Puzhen Engineering Section of the Jinpu Railway. Zhen: Zhen Shufang, a clerk in the compilation and inspection section of the Jinpu Railway General Office, is from Penglai, Shandong. Chang Jin Yuan, from Tianjin, Hebei, is a ticket inspector on the Jinpu Railway. Ji Yantian, with the style name Ligeng, from Jiaohe, Hebei, and Gou Zhongxian, with the style name Gongwei, from Jiangning, Jiangsu, are both captains of the Jinpu Railway motorcade.

Several Surnames Outside the Hundred Family Surnames 180

— (Bo Shen) (Que Chou)

There have already been several articles discussing strange surnames; these surnames are indeed rare, and they have aroused the interest of many readers; I am also one of them; so I have collected several surnames outside the Hundred Family Surnames to contribute to the readers. Li Zhaolian, wrote a book called "Xiaoting Miscellaneous Records"; Zhan Shutang, is the current commander of the 81st Division; Tan Zixin, is the commander of the 10th Cavalry Division in Henan; Lai Siyong, is from Xiaoshan, Zhejiang, and is currently in the same school as me; Jing Zhaoqian, is the current commander of the 29th Army Gendarmerie; La Qingzhang, is from Chengdu, Sichuan; You Guocai, is the current director of the Civil Affairs Department of Guizhou; Yuan Songzhou, was a member of the Jiangsu Disaster Investigation Group more than ten years ago; Da Qingbao, is from Liuhe, Jiangsu, and is also in the same school as me; Guo Hailan, is a special commissioner for banning tobacco cultivation, currently in Fujian; Cheng Guanyou, is a staff member of the Tongchang Pawnshop in Suzhou, I don't know if he is still there; Fu Zhifang, is a classmate of the author's friend, Mr. Qian.

Strange Surnames Talk 181

— (A Corner)

In my hometown of Chaozhou, there are quite a few unusual surnames. In Raoping County, there's a compound surname, (Wu Xu). The famous Dr. Zhang Jingsheng's ex-wife was named Wu Xu Chunjiang, who studied at the provincial second normal school. Her relatives are numerous. Some suggest that people with the surname Wu were adopted by the Xu family, and later their surname became these two characters, Wu Xu. This cannot be definitively determined. It's probably somewhat similar to Lufei Bohong of the China Medical Bureau and Ma Xu Weibang, the movie star. In Raoping, there's also a village where everyone is surnamed (Zhan), which is also very special. In Zhanglin Town, Chenghai County, there are many overseas Chinese surnamed (Yi). In Shantou, there's a tea shop called Yi Xing Ji. This large signboard attracts a lot of attention. According to them, their ancestors were two sworn brothers who gathered clams by the sea. They added the insect radical to the character for righteousness (義) to form their own clan. This is probably just unfounded rumor. In fact, this surname does exist. I've seen it in Shanghai, but written in the ancient form 螘, it seems more elegant. In Guangzhou, there's a strange surname (　), pronounced the same as Xuan. Among the members of the Guangdong natives in Shanghai Association, there are Bu Wenze, Ying Siyou, Lao Yanlin, and a Ms. Xing Shunhua. These surnames are also rare. Also, my friend Pan Jinzhai writes the upper part of his surname Pan with the character for "rice" (米), becoming (潘), instead of the "collect" radical (采). It's said that it's a branch of the Pan surname, so he is very careful when printing business cards, insisting on lithography. Because if it's printed with lead type, a stroke would have to be removed from the cast character, which is unsightly. This is similar to the You surname in Shanghai. In the phone book, besides the You character (尤), there's also a You character with a dot less (尢), divided into three strokes and four strokes. If you don't know this, you won't be able to find Mr. You even if you search the book thoroughly. In fact, both are pronounced as You. There are the most unusual surnames in the theater world. As far as I know, there are quite a few in Beijing. For example, the leading male actors Gui Junqing, Ming Haishan, Pu Youan, Zhi Heqing, Guan Dayuan, Shi Huibao, En Xiaofeng, the young male actor De Junru, the martial actor Chi Yueting, Rui Debao, the painted-face actor Mei Ne Shaoxian, Qing Chunpu, Ju Dekui, Fu Xiaotian, the clown Ci Ruiquan, and the female lead Ru Shihui. Da Tianbei, a senior actor in Shanghai's new drama scene, is now a translator in the Hongkou police station. In Shanghai, the unusual surnames on shop signs are Ren Changtai Incense Candle Shop and Yu Zhentai Silver Shop, which everyone knows. There's a paper shop called Xing He Tai in the Nanshi area. Its owner's surname is Xing. Perhaps you haven't noticed. This can be said to be an unusual surname among the "Three Tai" in Shanghai. My friend Wang and Ren went to the Commercial Press to print business cards. Because the manuscript was written sloppily, he had the Wang character printed as Ren (壬), probably thinking it was related to Ren Yutai. Moreover, it has some connection with the Ren character in his name, so he didn't notice the mistake. Some people say: the fewer strokes a surname has, the better, like Ding and Bu. They are often listed at the top when listing names. If your surname is Yi (一), wouldn't that be great? In fact, Yi is also a surname. According to the Kangxi Dictionary, there was a Yi Xuanzong in the Ming Dynasty. Not only is there a surname with the character Yi, but there's also a surname with the character Liu (六). My friend Zhou Wenxi saw Liu Ziming on the staff attendance sheet and asked him if it was Lu or Yue, why write a different character? In fact, there was indeed this surname in the Warring States period. Another friend, Cai Jianhen, hired a wet nurse. She said her surname was Qi (懎), and he thought it was the Chang of Changzhou. I said this might be a descendant of the Qi from the Zuo Zhuan, because Qi and Qi are the same character.

My Talk About Strange Surnames 182

— (Qing Qu)

In my Jiading city, there used to be a dim sum shop. One of its owners was surnamed (Yuan). Everyone pronounced this (Yuan) as "Gu." His shop's name was originally (Yuan De Sheng), so he was called "Gu De Sheng." Outside the West Gate, there's a paper shop that prints Buddhist images (shenmo). Its owner was surnamed (Ze), named (Huaqing), but he has now passed away. In Guangfu, there's someone surnamed (Qiang), whose nickname is (Zisheng). He runs a rice shop in Shanghai, and is the eldest manager of the Xie Chang De business. Last year, the branch director of the Nanxiang Public Security Bureau was surnamed (Bi), named (Xiuzhao). It's really rare to encounter someone surnamed (Bi). I'm afraid that apart from this branch director, you wouldn't find him anywhere else!

I once met a friend in Shanghai and asked his surname. He said it was (Xin). When I first heard it, I couldn't figure out the pronunciation, and thought it must be a variant of (Sun) or a mistaken form of (Xun), because he was from the north. I couldn't be sure. Later, he took out a card from his pocket, on the back of which were printed two lines of small red characters: (Shunian), styled Yougu, a successful candidate in the imperial examination from Dong'an, Shuntian). Only then did I understand that this friend was surnamed (Xin), named (Shunian), and styled (Yougu), a former scholar. Also, in the third prison of Shanxi, there was a section chief who asked someone to buy life insurance in Shanghai a few years ago. His surname was really strange, (Ti), named (Renfu). Not only was the pronunciation hard to say correctly, but when I looked it up in the dictionary, I found out his surname was (Ti), pronounced like "Ti." There was also someone surnamed (Duo) with whom I had worked. But I can't remember that friend's name anymore. He seemed to be from Yunnan, and his father, named (Ruzheng), was a successful candidate in the imperial examination in the year of Bingzi. It is rare indeed to see someone surnamed (Duo)!

One day, I flipped through a commemorative album of a certain company, and there were many strange surnames inside, such as (Zhi Yiqi), (Chu Buzhou), (Mou Shenxiu), (Da Yaoxian). These four surnames are also rare. Among the five elements, besides the surnames (Jin) and (Shui), I haven't seen (Mu) and (Tu). Only in the newspaper I often see Mr. (Huo Xueming) writing articles. In that case, a surname (Huo) is indeed a rare one!

Small Poems from the Lodging House, Rhyming with Yu Gang and Respectfully Sending to Jiping 183

— Yang An

My small dwelling is isolated from the noise, opening the window reveals the new green of the willows. I live in leisure, accompanied by flowers, and we are neighbors on fine nights. A little wine doesn't hurt to get drunk, cherishing the spring with affection. I have no other attachments, and cherish this body through the cold years.

In Late Spring of Yi Hai, I Invited Qi Zhang, Yu Gang, Wei Yubo, and Other Gentlemen for a Drink, but Bo Wei Did Not Arrive. I Obtained These Lines and Finished Them. 184

— Yang Mang

Light shade and drizzle wash away the dust of the streets, a single gathering shows true character. Quick events, quick people, create quick words, good friends and good companions enjoy a drunken good time. Clear words almost make one want to repeat them three times, fine wine - why not risk drinking a hundred cups? The trees are old and the spring is deep, the poetic intent is faint, let us seek another gathering to entertain the guests.

Strange Surnames of Classmates 185

— Huang Tian

This journal has published articles by Mr. Wan Gong and Mr. Gong Min about unusual surnames, which seem very interesting. I happen to have a yearbook of classmates at hand, so I flipped through it and found a few unusual surnames as well. Now I'll write them out to join in the fun. "La" - from Zhechuan, Henan. "Qu" - from Muping, Shandong. "Shui" - from Jiading, Jiangsu. "Zhang" - from Funing, Jiangsu. "Ju" - from Taiyu, Jiangsu. "Shi" - from Shouxian, Anhui. "Gou" - from Sichuan. "Qie" - from Sichuan. These are all very rare surnames. Especially the last two, if one Mr. Gou and another Ms. Qie were to marry, these two "honorable surnames" put together would be truly wonderful.

When I was in elementary school, I had a classmate whose surname was "Chi". According to a classmate from Yunnan, there used to be a division commander in Yunnan whose surname was "Na." It is said that the ancestors of this "Na" division commander were Tibetans. Nowadays, some people in Guangxi are surnamed "Ji." According to the locals in Guangxi, those with the surname "Ji" are the truly original people of Guangxi. Some people in Guangxi are also surnamed "Nong," said to be descendants of the Southern Man king Nong Zhigao.

Collecting strange surnames is not just an interesting thing. Every strange surname must have its origin. It's likely that there are more strange surnames in the border provinces, which is due to mixing with other ethnic groups. If the genealogy of each strange surname is studied to see its origin, it would be a very meaningful work in anthropology.

Various Strange Surnames 186

— Xiang Xian

Recently, this journal has been discussing the topic of "strange surnames" with great enthusiasm, starting with Mr. Wan, followed by Mr. Gong and Mr. Liu. I, Xiang Xian, though unworthy, also come to "attach to the tail of the horse," so to speak, to further make the event a success. I wonder if Mr. Shou Juan, the "uncrowned emperor" of the newspaper, "thinks so"? (Thank you for making me the emperor, but I'm afraid of revolution and the guillotine, so I dare not accept it, the editor jokingly notes.) I remember what I learned in my studies and the discoveries of unusual surnames among my classmates over the past ten years. So I'll write them down as follows:

"Qin" Qin Huali, a disciple of Mo Di, once studied under Zixia, and was mentioned alongside Mo Di. "Lie" Liezi, named Yukou, a man of Zheng, lived at the same time as Duke Mu of Zheng, and wrote eight chapters, called Liezi. "Gu" Notes from Jingzhai: "...Bu merchant Gu Ziming, strong and powerful, resisted the bandits, and was spared from the disaster." "Dian" Dian Wei, a famous general of Wei during the Three Kingdoms period, was a confidant of Cao Cao. "Guan" Guan Ying, a scholar-official of the Han Dynasty, harmed Jia Yi and lost his position as a senior official, he is the one. "Jing" Jing Cha, a Chu poet, became famous after Qu Yuan drowned himself in the Miluo River. "Lu" Lu Wenshu, a court historian of the Han Dynasty. "Xi" Xi Chang, Biographies of Immortals: "Xi Chang was a minister of Zhou... later he went to the quicksands with Lao Tzu." "E" E Lai, a minister of the Shang Dynasty, Records of the Grand Historian: "E Lai was strong and served the king with his strength." "Xian" Xian Zishuo, along with Gao He, was a tyrant of Qi, banished from his hometown, studied under Mozi, and became a famous figure in the world. "Zou" Zou Yan, Records of the Road says: "Descendants of the lesser lord of Zhu, in the Zhou Dynasty there were Zou Yan, Zou Ji, and Zou Shi, known as the Three Zous." "Zai" Analects: "Zai Wo asked about the length of the three-year mourning period." Zai Wo is also written as Zai Yu, a disciple of Confucius. "Wei" Weizi Qi, the half-brother of the Shang Dynasty tyrant Zhou, Zhou was licentious and did not listen to his advice, so he left. The Duke of Zhou advised Wu Geng to order Weizi to replace the Shang Dynasty, and he was enfeoffed in Song. "Li" Li Zhu, a man of the Yellow Emperor's time, could see the tip of an autumn hair from a hundred paces, Mencius wrote Li Lou. "Shi" Shi Kuang, a minister of Jin, could summon ghosts and spirits with his music. "Hui" Hui Shi, a debater of the Six Kingdoms period, his learning came from "separate Mo." "Ku" Ku Huo, Zhuangzi, All Under Heaven: "...The Ku Huo of the South, Ji Chi, and Dengling Zi, all recited the Mo Canon." "　"　Cuo, a man of Yingchuan in the Han Dynasty, studied the criminal law of Shen Buhai and Shang Yang. He was a tutor of the crown prince during the reign of Emperor Wen, and was favored for his eloquence. Later, when the Seven Kingdoms of Wu and Chu rebelled, Emperor Jing used Yuan Ang's words to kill Cuo in the East Market. "Pen" Pen Che, a native of Shanxi, a classmate in the past, quick-witted, but unfortunately died young. "Shan" Shan Linsheng, a farmer of my family, a native of Huaibei, many of his clan are lost. "Cui" Cui Huaren, a native of Yongning, Guangxi, also a former classmate, I don't know where he went after graduation. Recently, I read the Da Ri Bao, which published a list of lawyers in Shanghai, there is a Bian Jialu, this surname is not common. The latest famous movie star Diao Banhua, this surname is also not common. Also, in Mr. Liu's article "Talking about Surnames" on the 12th, there is an entry for the "Ling" clan, with a note: This newspaper often has a contributor called Ling Hu Zhao. According to Ling Hu Zhao is the pen name of my classmate Mr. Shen, not his real surname, and should be deleted when someone compiles a "Record of Strange Surnames" in the future.

I think the "strange surnames" published in the newspaper for several days in a row have research value, so I specially come to contribute a few surnames for the reference of the readers:

Yesterday, although foreign banks continued to soar in the silver market, the mood was still lacking in significant impact. However, due to Western merchants restricting the supply of foreign exchange, it was difficult to tighten. Furthermore, the Dalian speculators heavily shorted, creating a new low of $758.50. In the morning, with overseas foreign markets continuing to soar, but with big speculators on the ground, the market slightly sang the New York silver price has increased to 77 cents, which has reached the stipulated price. The Monterrio forward silver price soared by 3 points, and exchange rates all shrank. London bullion rose 8 and a half pence. Although the local market was stimulated, there was a lack of sellers after the dip, and the fall was not enough. The off-market pre-market opened, falling to $734. Buyers flocked in, and it rose to $80. Then large players began to sell bars, and it fell back to $734. Many people took advantage of the low price to cover their short positions, and it rose again. The Central Bank announced its listing, with both the British and American currencies rising, and the customs gold unit falling by 1.2%. The standard price of margin fell to $840.90, and then it weakened slightly. After the opening, banks tried to restrict the shilling, and the exchange rate hardened and fell, but did not break the $70 mark. Buyers took advantage of the low price to become active, gradually pushing it up. Short sellers rushed to cover their positions, and it briefly rebounded. Unfortunately, this did not last long. Jewish merchants Qiao Zhifu and Sassoon both came to restrict supply, and the exchange rate loosened and fell again. The white silver equilibrium tax remained unchanged and retreated within $70. Sassoon and Qiao Zhifu restricted again, and the domestic shilling was incredibly hard, falling to $763. Unexpectedly, both the Associated Press and Reuters reported that our ambassador to the United States, Shi Zhaoji, protested to US Secretary of State Hull about raising silver prices, which caused a brief reaction, rebounding by more than $10. However, because Sassoon was still selling foreign exchange, the domestic market was still hard, and it soon fell again. At noon, it hovered around $70. In the afternoon market, the market turned from flat to weak, falling within the $70 mark. Selling pressure increased sharply and it fell. Indian silver was reported to have risen 45 annas, once approaching the $60 mark. The exchange market was normal, and there was no shortage of short covering after the fall, so there were repeated rebounds. Indian silver rose again by 9 annas for the second time. Although there was downstream, it soon stabilized, because Reuters reported that the Indian silver market had stopped new transactions and was only allowed to settle. However, the Dalian speculators worked hard to dump, finally breaking the $60 mark and falling to a new price of $758.50. Finally, Indian silver contracted back by 9 annas for the third time, and buyers were strong again. The exchange rate also improved because of some telephone purchases from Bombay, and the situation improved. Finally, it presented a hovering situation. Spot prices will diverge from margin, and adding water will become even more expensive. The spot market posted $9 premium due to short covering. After today's market situation is recorded.

Yesterday, it was estimated that 150 bags of Andong beans were opened at a price of 4.92 yuan, more than 100 bags of Sipingjie beans at a price of 4.4 yuan, more than 200 bags of Hankou Zha beans at a price of 3.81 yuan, more than 240 bags of Hankou Chi beans at a price of 3.7 jiao and 5 jiao 9. As for foreign countries, only Dongzhuang Road is available, but unexpectedly, it has also stagnated. There are very few inquiries, so it is going downhill step by step, with a downward trend. It is heard that yesterday the price of bran in each market was as low as 2.28 yuan.

Shen Bao Wireless Radio Weekly

Shortwave Components 202

— Jiang Shengshi

(1) General Remarks

The success of a shortwave radio often depends on the quality and effectiveness of its components. Some components that are very suitable for broadcast radios cannot be used for shortwave reception. This article does not discuss the design of shortwave radios or their components, but hopes to provide some help to readers when choosing components.

Figure 1A is a very common parallel resonant circuit in radios. At first glance, the circuit seems simple, with only an inductance L and a capacitance C. However, upon closer examination, it is not so simple. At resonance, the impedance of L is 2πfL, and the capacitive impedance of C is 1/(2πfC), which are balanced. At this time, the current in the circuit can be obtained by Ohm's law, just as in a DC circuit:

In a parallel circuit, R represents the equivalent ohmic resistance applied to the circuit (Figure 1B).

We know that the current is maximum at resonance. If we multiply it by the impedance of L or C, we get the voltage between terminals A and B in the figure, which is input to the vacuum tube. However, in reality, the coil and capacitor have losses, so R cannot be ignored. Any current flowing through R results in energy loss. The purpose of shortwave components is to minimize this equivalent resistance, in other words, to reduce the loss of this circuit.

The voltage amplification factor of this resonant circuit is often equal to the ratio of the coil impedance 2πfL to the resistance R. Therefore, the smaller R is, the greater the amplification factor. However, it must be noted that the value of R varies with frequency and is not constant. Therefore, in practice, the same amplification factor cannot be obtained for many different frequencies.

(2) Reducing Dielectric Loss

High-efficiency shortwave coils can be made smaller to limit the external electric field. The support for winding the coil must be chosen with low dielectric loss.

The coil can be wound on a ribbed support to keep the wire as far away from the support as possible.

Also, when a coil and a capacitor are connected in parallel as shown in Figure A, it is found that the resonant frequency of the circuit itself is not

but lower than this value. This is because the coil L is not purely inductance, but also has a small amount of capacitance. There is capacitance between each turn of the coil. Therefore, a coil actually contains many small capacitances in series, which are distributed between the conductors of the coil. Thus, at high frequencies, part of the current does not flow through the coil, but bypasses it, resulting in loss. This capacitance can be regarded as being connected in parallel with capacitor C, thus increasing its resonant wavelength. This capacitance is called the coil's self-capacitance. If its value is C1, then the true resonant frequency of this matching circuit is

To reduce this loss, a gap equal to several times the diameter of the conductor can be left between each turn of the coil to minimize its self-capacitance.

The number of turns of the grid coil should be such that it can be matched with the tuning capacitor to obtain the required waveband. If a regenerative coil is needed, then the smaller the better, so that it can just oscillate to reduce its impact on the tuning coil. In general, the regenerative coil is about half or one-third of the grid coil. (To be continued)

A New Method for Radio Stations to Solicit Listener Opinions 203

— Pao

The programs of a radio station naturally change according to the opinions of the listeners. The usual method for radio stations to solicit listener opinions is through correspondence. This method is time-consuming, and most listeners are too lazy to write letters, so the results are naturally not good. Using the telephone to solicit opinions is also inappropriate, because if all the listeners call at the same time, the radio station will not be able to cope. Therefore, wireless experts have been engaged in research to solve this difficulty, and preliminary work has now been completed.

One day, after a music program on American radio station WRO, the announcer reported: "Please turn on a 40-watt light bulb if you are listening to this station's programs in this city, and turn it off immediately after turning it on." A few minutes later, the announcer reported: "Please turn on a light bulb in the same way if you like this program." Finally, the announcer asked those who did not like this program to turn on a light bulb. (As shown in Figures A and B) In less than a minute, the radio station already knew that 10% of the 60,000 people in the local area were listening, and 95% of those listening at this time were satisfied with this program.

This new method of soliciting opinions was invented by radio expert Hopkins of New York. The principle is very simple. When thousands of listeners turn on a light bulb at the same time, the load of the power plant will naturally change greatly. This change is recorded by an "automatic recorder" (as shown in Figures C and D). The broadcasting station has a special auxiliary automatic recorder. From the size of the three changes recorded by this recorder, the radio station can calculate the answers to the above three questions, in other words, it can know the opinions of the listeners.

In addition, Hopkins has also designed a "wireless election recorder" to record the number of votes for or against a motion during a meeting. (Of course, it can also be used for other equivalent purposes) The principle is also very simple: a shortwave antenna is installed in front of the seats of the members; a shortwave transmitter is installed behind it to transmit radio waves; each member has a small rod with a single-turn loop coil on it and a button on the handle; when the button is pressed down, the coil becomes a closed circuit, and part of the radio waves is absorbed, and the radio waves received by the antenna in front of the seat are reduced; the amount of this reduction can be read from a specially made meter, and the number of people who oppose or support the motion can be known.

Radio is evolving, and new uses and new devices are discovered every day. We must work hard to study it.

Attached Figure A, the announcer asks questions to solicit listener opinions; B, listeners express their opinions according to the law; C, the automatic recorder in the power plant records the opinions of the listeners; D, a page of the recording, the highest peak represents the number of listeners at that time, the middle peak represents the number of people who agree, and the lowest peak represents the number of people who oppose.

Steps for Assembling a Radio for Beginners 208

— Xuelun

Beginners in assembling radios often suffer from the large number of new vacuum tube models and lack the ability to choose, resulting in unsuccessful reception. Therefore, I have written an article on the knowledge that beginners should have, which has been published in this newspaper. Due to the limited space, the circuit diagrams have not been published one by one, and I am afraid that beginners cannot fully understand them. Therefore, I will explain the expansion method and the circuit diagrams in detail again, as a reference when assembling radios.

When designing a radio, the first thing to solve is the power supply problem. As mentioned before, for the sake of convenience, only the 6.3-volt vacuum tube is drawn and explained. This type of vacuum tube is a car tube, which is sturdy, economical, durable, and consumes very little power. Therefore, it is suitable for both AC and DC use, which is more convenient than other types of vacuum tubes.

Now, assume that we are designing a radio that will be expanded to one stage of high amplification, one stage of detection, one stage of high-power low amplification, and one stage of rectification. The vacuum tubes used are No. 39 or 44 for high amplification, No. 36 or 37 for detection, No. 38 or 42 for high-power low amplification, and No. 80 for full-wave rectification. It is best to use an aluminum plate for the chassis, but dry plywood can also be used. The size of the chassis and the position of the parts are shown in Figure 1. The expansion positions for the future have been reserved one by one. It is best to purchase a double-gang variable capacitor for adjusting the frequency.

(1) Starting to Assemble a Single-Tube Radio

A single-tube radio uses a power amplifier tube for louder volume, but it is necessary to change the circuit when adding high and low amplification stages, so it is simpler to use a detector tube directly. Now, a No. 36 screen-grid tube is used for detection, and feedback is used to adjust the screen voltage to control it, so the oscillation is stable and the sensitivity is higher than that of No. 37. The wiring method is shown in Figure 2.

L uses a spider web board with an inner diameter of 1 and 1/4 inches, wound with 12 turns of No. 28 enameled wire. The starting end is grounded, that is, a solder lug is used to fix it on the screw of the spider web board, and the ending end is connected to the antenna.

L1 uses a spider web board of the same size as above, wound with 84 turns of the same enameled wire. The starting end is grounded as above, and the ending end is connected to the fixed plate of the variable capacitor.

L2 uses a spider web board of the same size as above, wound with 30 turns of the same enameled wire. The starting end is connected to the screen grid, and the ending end is connected to the high-impedance choke.

C a 0.00035 microfarad double-gang variable capacitor, Zhongyong No. 2221, with a slow-motion dial.

C1 a 0.00025 microfarad grid capacitor, produced by Zhongyong or Xinji.

C2 a 0.0005 microfarad bypass capacitor, produced by Xinji.

R 2 megohm grid leak, produced by American.

R1 100,000 ohm potentiometer, used to adjust the volume, must be produced by top-grade European and American manufacturers.

RFC 85,000 Henry high-frequency choke, produced by American or Zhongyong.

V a No. 36 vacuum tube, produced by Erxi'ai or Leisheng, with a five-pin lower tube socket.

After the parts are assembled, they can be fixed with screws according to the position in Figure 1, and then welded firmly one by one according to the circuit in Figure 2. The three spider web boards are separated by insulating paper and stacked and nailed to the bottom. If the feedback is too strong, the number of turns of L2 can be removed, and vice versa. A transformer for electric bells, a 6-volt battery, or four dry batteries can be used to supply A power. B power should first use 90V dry batteries. If this machine is assembled correctly, a 5-inch speaker can be used to listen to the central and local radio stations. (To be continued)
