Bible Sales in China Greatly Increased 212

— Li Min

In China, which is suffering from natural disasters, man-made calamities, internal troubles, and foreign invasions, it is unexpected that sales of the Bible have been particularly good. According to reports, the British and Foreign Bible Society reported that Bible sales in China last year were particularly good, an increase of 394,200 copies compared to 1933, with a total of 4,296,495 copies sold. From a business perspective, this cannot but be considered good news.

The reason why Bible sales were particularly good in China last year is that, on the one hand, it proves that the Chinese people are generally living in dire straits, with no way out. They can only use the Bible as a place of comfort and sustenance, seeking spiritual anesthesia. This may be the reason why Bible sales were particularly good in China last year. However, because Bible sales were particularly good, the Chinese people are hoping to find their ideal paradise in their minds, thus forgetting the immediate pain. This may not be very good news for the future of the Chinese nation. The Chinese nation now seems to need a tonic rather than an ideal paradise.

Last year, Bible sales were not only particularly good in China, but also increased in other countries. According to reports, Germany increased by 1,900 copies. This further illustrates how people in various countries, under the suffering of the current situation, hope to be able to reach their ideal paradise. However, this paradise is always difficult to reach. How do people around the world push the pain of reality out of their minds? This has become a problem.

The general increase in Bible sales around the world does not prove that the people of the world are making progress and their thinking is getting better, but on the contrary, it shows the suffering and decadence of the people of the world. However, can the Bible ultimately save their souls? This is hard to say. Perhaps some people are taking the flesh of Jesus as bread and the blood of Jesus as wine. We see how many people have buried themselves for this thing. The Bible is being used by some people like guns and cannons, and it has achieved some effects of world stability. Its welcome is not accidental.

However, a cool sedative cannot in fact heal our wounds all over our bodies. What will the result be?

At Yijiang Tower 213

— Yan

The official river rushes out of the city gate under the drawbridge, turns a corner, and flows to Lower Pond. Yijiang Tower is located at the intersection of the rapids. The tallest building in the entire county is built on a stone dam. However, this is not a famous scenic spot. There are only a few firewood boats coming in and out of the river. The grand name of Yijiang was only thought of one day by the old teahouse customers, and the horizontal plaque was hung up like that.

Every day, the people who come to the Yijiang Teahouse are some of the most important people in the county. They bring their own reclining chairs or sleeping couches, and the teapots and tea leaves are also kept by the tea masters according to their own preferences. Their arrival at the teahouse is like going to the office at a fixed time. The tea masters remember it most clearly. If there is an unexpected visitor, he can predict that a certain master will arrive in a few minutes. If a young master or lord does not come to the teahouse for two days, the tea master will pay a visit on the third morning, and in the afternoon he will report the results of his investigation to the other lords. It is natural that ordinary people cannot be competent in this skill of the tea master. He was a follower of a county magistrate during the Qing Dynasty, and now he is over fifty years old. It is said that he spent a considerable amount of money to take over the stove of Yijiang Tower, so in addition to pleasing those lords, he also has amazing money-making skills.

Every spring, when the lords' gambling interest declines, probably after the Lantern Festival, Yijiang Tower always has new tricks brought in from the small pier, such as improved Shanghai opera, Suzhou opera, or female storytelling, to add to the lords' high spirits when they are interested. As for the authorities who maintain morality, the lords have already taken care of them. Every night, the electric lights on the floor are bright, there are sharp, delicate voices singing, and there are loud voices laughing. Several black-clothed policemen dragging batons appear next to the stairs, drinking free fragrant tea leaves, and when they hear something they like, they cannot help but laugh loudly, forgetting their own duties completely.

This year, the gambling game unexpectedly extended to the middle of February. Although the commission is also a considerable amount of money, the tea master tries every day to stop the gambling game, as he has arranged a very profitable trick. He discussed it with the most powerful lord, and the next day he started talking. He said that the daughter of Hua Xiaorong, who had been here before, has now grown up to be even more beautiful. He said that his wife saw her at some pier. He said that the teahouse prevents later listeners from entering every day. He said that Hua Xiaorong wants to come to the local area again. He said, do you lords like to listen?

Sure enough, this news aroused great attention from the lords in the game. They remembered Hua Xiaorong's smile. At that time, her child was only ten years old, more beautiful than her mother. Some calculated how old this child should be. The card game naturally stopped invisibly. Everyone went back to their recliners and pondered their own plans. The old looked at the young with jealous eyes, and the young looked at the old with jealous eyes. They all wanted to take that girl into their hands.

Although in the temporarily quiet air, a lustful atmosphere more lively than the card game can be estimated in every restless heart. Finally, the lords with whom the tea master had previously discussed naturally spoke.

"Is it the child called Hua Xiaoxiang?"

The tone was so weak, as if he didn't care about this matter. The tea master had already put on a smiling face and deliberately lowered his voice to say softly: "Yes! That little girl really has something, much more beautiful than her mother!"

The long trailing sound was sent into the two ears of every lord from the air. Their hearts were burning hot, but no one wanted to agree first.

"Are you still interested in gambling?" Still weakly, but without waiting for anyone to answer, he said again, "That's good too, let's change the taste."

"Yes!" the tea master shouted.

Returning Guest 214

— Jingyun

"Mom, Ah Hua in Flower Lane, she scolded me: 'Your dad is a bad person, a poor bum, he doesn't have money to buy you a toy train!' Mom, is dad really a bad person? Why doesn't he bring me a toy train from 'Fanbang' that is bigger and better-looking than Ah Hua's?"

Ah Yin, the eldest daughter of Shou Xingge, is about seven years old. Her cheeks are as red as the Guan Lord in the Guan Emperor Temple. Panting, she came from Flower Lane all the way to the pigsty behind the house, with two strings of tears hanging from the corners of her eyes. She can't stand Ah Hua's ridicule. In her eyes, she feels that Ah Hua is now very proud, with a novel and fun toy train. However, Ah Hua's dad and her dad are both "Fan Keq," so why doesn't dad bring her a toy train that is bigger and better-looking than Ah Hua's? This question keeps spinning in Ah Yin's childish heart. She pulls on the corner of her mother's clothes and complains repeatedly.

"Damn debtor, you're not young anymore, and you're still pestering me here. You don't have a dad, he's already dead… Go! Drive the ducks to the back pond to take a bath." The pigs in Mom's pigsty are so full that they are a little lazy. She puts down the bamboo ladle in her hand, turns her head, and points her heavy fingers hatefully on the top of Ah Yin's head. Her voice is like a broken bronze gong. Ah Yin cries out with a "wah" sound, and then her shadow disappears behind the house.

Whenever Ah Yin's dad is mentioned, Shou Xing's wife gets a little angry. She tightly resents Shou Xingge's ruthlessness. He has been "abroad" for seven or eight years, without sending a single letter home, let alone money. He left her and her daughter suffering at home. She always complains about her bitter fate, marrying an unenterprising husband, which has confined her at home for her whole life, suffering and letting her youth slip away. However, last month, the "water passenger" Ma Pi Lao Er from the village ran to her house to tell her that Shou Xingge had decided to take the next ship back to Tangshan. This sudden news unexpectedly made Shou Xing's wife feel infinitely happy. The dimples that she had not seen for a long time, which had died away, reappeared on her dark, thin face full of deep wrinkles.

Since Shou Xingge left her at home when Ah Yin was in her belly, he packed his simple luggage and went abroad. When he left, he also told her that he would soon ask the "water passenger" Ma Pi Lao Er to pick her up and take her to Fanbang to be happy. However, years had passed without any news, not even a letter of safety, as if a stone had sunk into the vast deep sea, with not a sound to be heard. This made Shou Xing's wife's heart as anxious as ants on a hot pot. She went several times to the homes of Fan Keq in the village who had just returned from Fanbang to inquire, but everyone said different things. Some said: "Shou Xingge has drifted to Bane to work as a 'piglet'!" Some said: "Shou Xingge has married a rich Fan woman and is living a happy life in Fanbang!" From then on, Shou Xing's wife guarded her daughter Ah Yin, living a gloomy and miserable life. She had no happy spring, no caring relatives. Except for her old mother, who came out of the mountains to visit them once in a long time, what accompanied them and supported them were those few pigs and a group of chickens and ducks. They were truly the most lonely and pitiful people in the world!

After the "water passenger" Ma Pi Lao Er came to her house to tell her the news that Shou Xingge was returning to Tangshan, she hurriedly washed the old furniture in the room, and from time to time a light smile would float on her face behind her back. Although she was still worried that Shou Xingge would bring back a beautiful and charming Fan woman to compete for her favor. However, when she thought that Shou Xingge would bring back at least a thousand or hundreds of shiny Fan Foreign coins in his suitcase this time, to relieve the years of resentment in her stomach, and let her live a comfortable life and show off her ambition in front of her relatives, it was after all beyond Shou Xing's wife's expectations. Shou Xingge still carried the simple luggage he had when he left and stepped into the house with a sick body.

"Why are you so embarrassed? My God!" Shou Xing's wife's dream turned into a bubble. "I am truly a bitter person!" Shou Xingge couldn't even say a word, and lay down on the newly washed bed, sighing frequently…

Random Gleanings from Late Spring 215

— Cheng Quan

(The express train tightly gripped the two parallel lines of the permanent track, frantically rushing towards the endless road: racing over hills, over embankments, over fields, over graveyards and orchards, over clusters of houses filled with contemplations.

It was dusk. The dim sky was crowded with heavy moisture. A cloudy day! Moreover, it was the dusk of a cloudy day—the dusk of a cloudy day, when even the most active and ardent sun in the universe was as gloomy as an ancient philosopher, hiding within layers of grey clouds, contentedly following the inevitable fate of decline that the laws of nature bestowed upon its twilight years. Everything was deathly still: peach blossoms, bearing the scorch marks of autumn, coldly drifted onto the water surface. Cuckoos, absentmindedly, cried out a couple of times with their aged voices. It was all too fast! All the good, golden dream-like days had swiftly reached their end: the sun had set, and spring was also ending.

Moreover, this was a spring with few good days. Was it not? The entire spring had passed by in constant wind and rain; the mud on the ground, the mud in people's hearts too—some said: in this era, it is difficult to have good days? In this era, even spring is not worth pursuing or lamenting.)

Therefore, I attempted to quickly forget my own difficult youthful days, and the worthless, regretful mourning for the past "golden age."

When seeing people dissolving their proud youth in silver-toned romances, in the mesmerizing sounds of the "saxophone" in jazz music, in the great halls of learning that form the pyramid of knowledge, or in the excessive enjoyment of glamorous life, I almost began to doubt whether I myself had ever possessed the blessing of what is called youth—just like a native of the northern lands, who grew up in a rainy region, upon entering a place bathed in sunlight all year round, becomes stunned and dumbfounded.

Indeed, the rain and muddy gloom of the northern lands are hard to compare with the "gentle breezes and bright sunshine" of the south. Similarly, how can someone who has stumbled through a grey, windy, and difficult spring (a once-in-a-lifetime spring!) imagine the possibility of brightness in another world?

Is it useless to talk about regret and lament? Yes. But even those who stroll in spring, when caught in a dismal spring and their interest wanes, still regret the waste of their travel expenses. Moreover, one's own travel expenses are life—life!

In this world, are there not many poets and philosophers who have exhausted their efforts to explain to us the preciousness of youth? However, this is of no use to people living in another world. When a person accepts the instinct for survival bestowed by nature, and on the other hand, accepts the congenital misfortune bestowed by society, thus carrying a small soul, and beginning the long journey of their life, who can still be in the mood to chant about the spring scenery?

Thus, using small and feeble steps, stepping step by step through muddy roads, and using all kinds of caution and tension to gather up a scale or a claw of the opportunities for life discarded by fortunate people, a precious youth quietly slips away, like playing hide-and-seek, like a night thief.

Finally, accidentally looking up: the grey gate of middle age stubbornly and gloomily stands before me, and I have already walked through the wind and rain to the end of youth, having consumed those days that will never return in the wind and rain.

Spring has already reached its twilight; thereafter, in the corridors of life, what else will I gather?…

A Grown Sparrow 216

— Hua Mu

(Now, there is no need to worry about this poor little sparrow any more. It is no longer afraid, stubborn, or hostile towards us. It obediently flutters its fragile fledgling wings, opens its small yellow beak, and swallows the food picked on the bamboo stick with a chirping sound. We are so happy that we almost want to jump for joy. This poor little life, perhaps, will grow up in this small bamboo cage, except for the physiological defects that we humans cannot provide for.)

Our joy is not due to chance or temporary curiosity. It was yesterday afternoon, after a gust of wind and rain, that we discovered a poor little sparrow, its water-soaked wings drooping, crouching under the fence, chirping sadly. We were immediately moved by this sound with a sense of surprise. When we reached out to catch it, a kind of fearful and angry light shot out from its small eyes, flapping its small wings and struggling. This made us hesitate for a moment and withdraw our hands. However, its ability to fly was ultimately too weak. Unwilling to watch a small life freeze and starve to death, we finally caught it and put it in a small bamboo cage.

It was very stubborn at first, jumping and dashing in the cage, looking very angry. When we walked away, it chirped again. We guessed it was hungry, so we picked some food on a bamboo stick and sent it to its mouth, trying to coax it to eat. But it didn't open its mouth to take it, flapping its wings and cowering in the corner of the cage, its small eyes staring blankly at us, and it stopped chirping. We tried all sorts of ways to coax it, but it didn't work. This made us very angry, so we held it in our hands and pried open its beak with one hand, stuffing the food in. Watching it try to stretch its neck as much as possible, swallowing the stuff stuck in its throat with eyes blinking, we worried that the future of this poor little life was very bleak.

But now, there's no need to worry. Look, it's no longer afraid, stubborn, or hostile towards us, chirping as if it sees us as its mother. Obediently fluttering its fragile wings, opening its small yellow beak, and taking the food picked on the bamboo stick with a chirping sound. When it is full, it quietly hides in its nest and dozes off; when it is hungry, it jumps out again, as if asking its mother for food.

We run to the fields every day to catch some small insects and then pick them one by one to feed it. We never feel bored or tedious; on the contrary, it adds a strong sense of beauty to this ordinary life. As the days go by, its feathers gradually become plump. We often let it out; it will fly from the tiles on this side to the trees outside the wall. Sometimes, it spreads its wings and lies on the tiles under the sun, blinking its eyes. That kind of leisurely expression really makes us happy and envious. As long as we whistle, it chirps and flies down again, landing on our hands or shoulders. We have never worried that it would fly away and not come back. What we worry about is not being able to catch green worms and the civet cat that is always lurking in the corner of the house.

As the days go by. The yellow on the little sparrow's beak has gradually faded. Sometimes we get angry at its mischievousness and cunning, hating that it is not as tame as usual, but we still don't think it will fly away and not come back. Because it still comes back to the bamboo cage at night.

But, this lovely little sparrow finally didn't fly back! It's been two days now. The cage is empty at night. We try whistling, although we can't see it flying out from the wall outside, shaking its tail and jumping on the tiles. However, its feathers are full, its wings are strong, and it can find fatter and more palatable green worms than we give it. It wants to use its young strength to soar in the vast and free world! It is already a grown sparrow.

How can there be such a bad marriage in the world? Talking about divorce makes one's heart ache. They have conflicting opinions and cannot live together. Some have children clinging to their clothes, and their tears don't dry. Some angrily turn their heads and willingly separate forever. Some are hypocritical and still want to flatter the beauty. Shenbao Local Supplement Film Special

Trivia about the Famous Clothes Rack, Adolphe Menjou 220

— Suyin

Adolphe Menjou, everyone knows he is French. Of course, he speaks French better than he speaks English. But when he was at Cornell University, the French professor actually failed him twice. Isn't that strange? But there are many strange things in Menjou's life, and we will slowly tell them.

His father originally ran a restaurant. Although he provided his son with a university education, his son, after graduating from university (it is not known whether Adolphe Menjou is a Cornell graduate), had to seek his own livelihood. Therefore, Adolphe ran to New York in 1913. At that time, he had only seven cents in his pocket. He wanted to enter the theater world. Coincidentally, he met a driver who introduced him to a theatrical affair. This was his first stage performance, with a salary of twenty-seven dollars and fifty cents per week.

He worked for a week, but he never got the twenty-seven dollars and fifty cents, because the troupe disbanded.

Later, in New York, he met a personnel director of the Justice Film Company. He promised him a job, but the company was in Florida, in the South. So he left New York and ran to Florida. The role he was going for required wearing a tuxedo. He didn't have a tuxedo. He used to borrow a tuxedo from his father's landlord, but now there was nowhere to borrow. His father gave him a diamond ring when he turned twenty-one. He was still wearing it on his hand at the time. He took it off and pawned it for sixty-five dollars.

With the sixty-five dollars, he made three tuxedos, which were morning dress, full dress, and dinner dress. He rented a small room and paid a week's rent. He had only five cents left. The next day, he excitedly ran to the Justice Film Company to report. But the film was announced to be suspended!

The Justice Film Company was on the eleventh floor, and on the seventh floor, there was the Vance Film Company. When he took the elevator down from the eleventh floor, he saw many people gathered in front of the Fox Company through the glass window, as if they were recruiting extras. So he took the elevator down and then took the elevator back up. Sure enough, Fox Company was going to shoot a French film. He stood in line, walking up one by one. Suddenly, a young man saw Menjou and shouted from afar: "Hey! You with the mustache! You go!" This was the beginning of his opportunity, which can be said to be a coincidence.

In the Fox Company, although he was just an ordinary extra, the company authorities gradually got to know him. One day, the famous director Townsend called him over, gave him a script, asked him to read it, and asked him if he could play that role. Menjou said: "Can I play it? I can eat it!" In this way, he was hired, and his salary suddenly jumped from five dollars a day to seventy-five dollars a week!

The rest is needless to say. But now he is a big star. Another thing that can be mentioned is that he is known in Hollywood for his exquisite clothing. He has countless clothes. According to his own estimate, he has about two hundred suits, about fifty coats, and countless shirts, hats, and shoes that he never sees once a year. But when he first arrived in Hollywood, he tried many ways to get a tailor to make him four suits, and the price was paid back in installments. Now, if any tailor gets Adolphe Menjou's patronage, it is a great honor, and the price is not a concern.

Another thing that can be mentioned is his name. You know, Adolphe Menjou is his real name. When he first entered the film industry, many people wanted him to change his name. A big director said: "If you don't succeed, it's your name that will ruin you. That name is too heavy." Van Miller begged him to change it, telling him that no one could remember Menjou. Many people said that when they saw the word, they didn't know how to read it. He said, "Jacob Braille! That's your name, it couldn't be better.

But Menjou said: "Jacob Braille, let him go to hell." Now he is famous, and not only can everyone pronounce his name according to German pronunciation, but it is also known to every household, and women and children all know it.

Don't get me wrong. Adolphe Menjou is not a extravagant person. He is known for his clothing, which is his way to fame, and a business strategy that must be maintained. He himself is very frugal. He doesn't use a secretary. He personally opens and answers all the fan letters. He also doesn't hire many servants. When someone asked him, he said humorously: "There are too many people, and there is not even a place for couples to quarrel peacefully."

He said that it is rare for couples to quarrel, but it is a bedroom pleasure!

Film Review

Review of "Carefree Gentleman" 221

— Ling He

—— Golden City Screening

In the dark movie theater, I accidentally heard a woman's voice saying:

"Not quite humorous, not quite comical, not quite bitter, not quite tragic." These two very ordinary sentences seem to be a very appropriate criticism of "Carefree Gentleman." Indeed, as a slapstick film, "Carefree Gentleman" hides a bitter life under the guise of laughter, which is not an ordinary artistic expression.

Anyone can understand that the playwright has great sympathy for people who are forced by hunger and cold. They are homeless, they wander on the streets, they need jobs, and they have good personalities. But the cruel society forces them to the brink of death. In the cold winter, they try their best to live on; however, the result is still disappointment.

Here, Liu Jiqun and Han Langen are O-shaped urban wanderers. They are kind, law-abiding, they have extravagant hopes for a luxurious or enjoyable life, they hope to get married, they need women, and they will do their best to serve Mei Lin, although what they can do cannot exceed a high degree of friendship. Similarly, they also feel dizzy when they see the chaotic crowd in the dance hall. In the end, they think that as long as they have a house that doesn't leak, they are already content. More cruelly, they dress up as monkey shows and ask people for sympathy, but all they get is five copper coins. However, the playwright also believes that people's conscience is not dead. Doctors or landlords are ultimately moved by their kindness.

What we feel satisfied with in this film is that the authors did not give the audience harmful poison. The authors have kind hearts, which make the audience feel emotional about life, but at the same time, they did not point out a clear path for the liberation of the lives of these kind people, but merely a beautiful yearning for the beautiful spring.

In terms of performance form, this fully expresses the author's deep understanding of film art. However, experience is inevitably unfamiliar, which we can see in all aspects. Here, we can rarely see Laurel and Hardy-style slapstick, but also rarely see the natural expression of tearful laughter. Similarly, the dubbing here, compared to other dubbed national films, is quite competent in the harmony between music and plot, but it is not an extremely skilled performance. In terms of Tempo, this is trying to make it better, but the director did not fully grasp it. Because the panning shots are too slow and too long, they seem unsuitable for the tone of comedy. Similarly, the two actors are not geniuses of comedy. Han Langen stiffly makes ugly faces, which is too much acting, setting off Liu Jiqun's performance as more humane. In addition, in editing, it commits the same problem of wordy accumulation as other national films. At least I think some places should be cut shorter.

Review of "The Decisive Moment" 222

— Hua Lun

Society Doctor——Nanjing Screening

I remember in Ibsen's play "An Enemy of the People," a doctor was criticized by society and even treated as a public enemy for proposing to improve the water supply of the bathhouse.

Here in "The Decisive Moment," a doctor is also depicted who, in order to save a critically ill patient, disregards the patient's father's opposition and resolutely performs surgery, ultimately saving the patient from danger. Although the story of this film does not narrate a hero like the one created by Ibsen, with such power, passion for social reform, and struggle against stubborn ideas, the form of the first half of the story does have some similarities. The difference lies in the essence. Ibsen's "An Enemy of the People" has a deeper and more thorough understanding, which lasts to the end. "The Decisive Moment" is narrow, and the doctor has little understanding. This is where one can distinguish the difference between serious Nordic artists and mediocre American writers.

The director's handling of this film, apart from the tension in the air during the surgery, has few successes to point out, but the control of the actors is acceptable. In addition, there are scenes such as the nurse secretly drinking and eating meat, and the doctor's drunken dance, which subtly suggest satire of the hospital and are quite meaningful.

CbestenMcrrio, who plays Dr. Mao Gen, has had considerable achievements in screen acting. He does not disappoint us in this film, but this story clearly limits him. Otherwise, I think he could have displayed his talent more. The remaining roles seem to be placed in secondary positions and cannot have any distinctive features.

"Falling Flowers Season" Premieres Today 223

The domestically produced blockbuster "Falling Flowers Season" is produced by Mingxing Film Company, directed by Wu Cun, and stars Xu Lai, Gong Jianong, Zhao Dan, Wang Xianzhai, Gu Meijun, Gu Lanjun, and others. The play depicts the situation of the defeated Northeast Volunteers, wandering in the city, struggling with life, interspersed with a love story, with a tortuous plot, centered on the falling flowers season of three eras. Mr. Wu's previous work "Bigamy" was released and was once honored as "Our Lubitsch." The excellent results of "Falling Flowers Season" can be imagined. It is now scheduled to be premiered at the Xingguang Grand Theatre on Ningbo Road starting today.

Small Records of Falling Flowers Season 224

…In Falling Flowers Season, there is a trench set with a depth and width of more than ten feet, which took five days to complete, which is the first time on the silver screen.

…Filming on location in Suzhou was delayed for twelve days due to rain before it was completed. Old Mouse Wu Cun scolded the God endlessly.

…Xu Lai, Gu Meijun, Gu Lanjun, Hu Jia, Shu Xiuwen, Huang Naishuang, etc., are all fashion model performers here.

…Gong Jianong and Zhao Dan had a fight over Xu Lai, each with several bruises on their faces after filming.

…Falling Flowers Season premieres at the Xingguang Grand Theatre starting today.

Movie Novel

Cloud Sky Hate Fills (Living on Velvet) 226

— Ti Yun

Just then, the doorbell rang. It was a streetcar conductor. Tuo Lei was talking when he saw the conductor come in, and he suddenly fell silent. He looked at Ai Mei, then at the conductor. He silently walked out. Ai Mei saw his expression and felt sad. She pointed to her purse and asked the conductor to put it in the car. She couldn't say a word. She walked towards the car parked at the door. Her eyes were blurred with tears, and she stumbled into the car.

Ai Mei left Tuo Lei and returned to her aunt's house, but she could not forget Tuo Lei at any moment. She spent her days like years. She forced herself to attend all the banquets. She forced herself to pretend to be happy. No matter where she was, she always laughed loudly, appearing happier than others, but only Hua De could see her inner pain. He knew that she was outwardly strong but inwardly weak, so every time he saw her, he felt sorry for her. He also often went to see Tuo Lei, wanting to reason with him, to stop his reckless flying, risking his life, but Tuo Lei laughed it off and continued to do as he pleased.

Later, Ai Mei could not bear it anymore. She could not live without Tuo Lei. But at this time, Tuo Lei no longer listened to other people's advice. Once, Ai Mei saw Tuo Lei driving Hua De's car past. She shouted at him from behind, but he stepped on the gas and sped away. The dangerous situation made her cover her face and dare not look, and she cried alone.

That night, Ai Mei's house was holding a banquet. Ai Mei wore the most beautiful clothes and displayed the most cheerful attitude. She was laughing and talking alone. She said, "Why shouldn't I be happy? Life is like morning dew, enjoy yourself while you can. I am now a person living in the clouds!" Many people who heard her words were puzzled and didn't know how to respond, they could only laugh along with her.

Suddenly, like a bolt from the blue, all the happiness disappeared. Hua De suddenly walked in. He walked up to Ai Mei and said in a trembling voice, "Ai Mei... I and you... need to go to a place... right now." Ai Mei looked at him for a moment and said faintly, "I know... it must be Tuo Lei... something went wrong..." Hua De couldn't help but lower his head. He said, "He drove my car... the police just called me... he got into trouble in a nightclub near here." Ai Mei listened, and without a word, followed him away.

Ai Mei didn't know how she arrived at this place. She only knew that Tuo Lei was injured. His body was lying horizontally on the ground in a pagoda in the center of the garden, motionless, his face as pale as paper. Ai Mei walked to his side and knelt down. Tuo Lei opened his eyes, looked around, and shook his head slightly impatiently, saying, "What are these people doing sneaking around... do they think I'm going to die... is that right? I won't die... when I'm going to die... I'll wait until I'm better... until I'm prepared... before I'm prepared, I won't die... no one can tell me when to die..."

Ai Mei held back her tears and comforted him, "Of course not, my love." Tuo Lei said again, "When I die, I must die in the sky... not on this dirty ground... the car won't take my life." Ai Mei said, "Of course not." (To be continued)
